"America" redirects here. For the landmass comprising North and South America, see [Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas "Americas"). For other uses, see [America (disambiguation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/America_\(disambiguation\) "America (disambiguation)").

Several terms redirect here. For other uses, see [US (disambiguation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_\(disambiguation\) "US (disambiguation)"), [USA (disambiguation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USA_\(disambiguation\) "USA (disambiguation)"), [United States (disambiguation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_\(disambiguation\) "United States (disambiguation)"), and [The United States of America (disambiguation)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_United_States_of_America_\(disambiguation\) "The United States of America (disambiguation)").

scope="row">Time zone</th><td><span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time">UTC</a>−4 to −12, +10, +11</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><div>•&nbsp;Summer&nbsp;(<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Daylight_saving_time">DST</a>)</div></th><td><span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time">UTC</a>−4 to −10<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-time-24"><span>[</span>g<span>]</span></a></sup></span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Date format</th><td>mm/dd/yyyy<sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>h<span>]</span></a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Calling code</th><td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_American_Numbering_Plan">+1</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_3166-2:US">US</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/.us">.us</a><sup><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>

The **United States of America** (**USA**), also known as the **United States** (**U.S.**) or **America**, is a country located primarily in [North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America").<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>j<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It is a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") of 50 [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state") and [the federal capital district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_district_of_the_United_States "Federal district of the United States") of [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.") The 48 [contiguous states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contiguous_states "Contiguous states") border [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada "Canada") to the north and [Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexico "Mexico") to the south, with the [semi-exclavic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-exclave "Semi-exclave") state of [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska") in the northwest and the [archipelagic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Archipelagic "Archipelagic") state of [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii") in the [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean"). [Indian country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_country "Indian country") includes 574 [federally recognized tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federally_recognized_tribes "Federally recognized tribes") and 326 [Indian reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_reservation "Indian reservation") with [tribal sovereignty rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_sovereignty_in_the_United_States "Tribal sovereignty in the United States"). The U.S. asserts sovereignty over five [major island territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and [various uninhabited islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands") in the Pacific Ocean and the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean"). It is an ecologically [megadiverse country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_country "Megadiverse country"), with the world's [third-largest land area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area")<sup id="cite_ref-largestcountry_15-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-largestcountry-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>c<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [third-largest population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population"), exceeding 340 million.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_clock_31-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-pop_clock-31"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>k<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[Paleo-Indians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleo-Indians "Paleo-Indians") migrated to North America across the [Bering land bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_land_bridge "Bering land bridge") more than 12,000 years ago, and formed [various cultures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_cultures_in_the_United_States "Native American cultures in the United States"). [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida"), the first [European colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas "European colonization of the Americas") in what is now the continental U.S., was established in 1513, and later [British colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") led to the first settlement of the [Thirteen Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies "Thirteen Colonies") in [Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia "Colony of Virginia") in 1607. Intensive agriculture in the rapidly expanding [Southern Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Colonies "Southern Colonies") encouraged the forced migration of [enslaved Africans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States "Slavery in the United States"). Clashes with the British Crown over taxation and political representation sparked the [American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution"), with the [Second Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress") formally declaring independence on July 4, 1776. The U.S. emerged victorious from the [American Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") of 1775 to 1783 and [expanded westward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny "Manifest destiny") across North America, dispossessing [Native Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States") during the [Indian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Indian_Wars "American Indian Wars"). The [Louisiana Purchase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase "Louisiana Purchase") in 1803 and the end of the [Mexican–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War "Mexican–American War") in 1848 saw significant territorial acquisition. As more states were admitted, a North–South division over slavery led to the secession of the [Confederate States of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America "Confederate States of America"), which fought [the Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_\(American_Civil_War\) "Union (American Civil War)") in the [American Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War") of 1861 to 1865. With the Union's victory, slavery was abolished nationally. In the late 19th century and early 20th century, the U.S. established itself as an industrial giant and [great power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_power "Great power") following the [Spanish–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanish–American War") and [World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_I "World War I"). After Japan's [attack on Pearl Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor") in 1941, the U.S. entered [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"); its aftermath left the U.S. and the [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union") as the world's [superpowers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower "Superpower"). During the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War"), both countries struggled for [ideological dominance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ideological_dominance "Ideological dominance") and [international influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence"). The Soviet Union's collapse and the end of the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War_\(1985%E2%80%931991\) "Cold War (1985–1991)") in 1991 left the U.S. as the world's sole superpower.

The [U.S. national government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States"), as established by the [Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States") in 1789, is a [presidential](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system") republic and [liberal democracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberal_democracy "Liberal democracy") with a separation of powers into three branches: [legislative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress"), [executive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_federal_executive_departments "United States federal executive departments"), and [judicial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_judiciary_of_the_United_States "Federal judiciary of the United States"). The [Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress"), the national legislature, is composed of the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives") (a lower house based on population) and the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") (an upper house based on equal representation for each state). [The federal system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_the_United_States "Federalism in the United States") provides substantial autonomy to the 50 states, each with its own constitution and laws. The American political tradition is rooted in [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment") ideals of liberty, equality, individual rights, and the rule of law. Since the 1850s, the [Democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_\(United_States\) "Democratic Party (United States)") and [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_\(United_States\) "Republican Party (United States)") parties have dominated [American politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_politics "American politics").

A [developed country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Developed_country "Developed country"), the [U.S. ranks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_rankings_of_the_United_States "International rankings of the United States") high in [economic competitiveness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report#2019_rankings "Global Competitiveness Report"), [productivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_productivity "List of countries by labour productivity"), innovation, and higher education. The U.S. accounted for [over a quarter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)") of nominal global economic output in 2024, and [its economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States "Economy of the United States") has been the world's [largest by nominal GDP since about 1890](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP"). It possesses the [largest amount of wealth of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_total_wealth "List of countries by total wealth") and has the highest [disposable household income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposable_household_and_per_capita_income#Disposable_income_per_capita_\(OECD\) "Disposable household and per capita income") per capita among [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") countries, though [U.S. wealth inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_inequality_in_the_United_States "Wealth inequality in the United States") is one of the most pronounced in those countries. A [melting pot](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Melting_pot "Melting pot") of [many ethnicities and customs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multiculturalism_in_the_United_States "Multiculturalism in the United States"), the [culture of the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States "Culture of the United States") has been shaped by centuries of immigration, and [its soft power influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americanization "Americanization") has a global reach. The U.S. is a member of [multiple international organizations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_organization_membership_of_the_United_States "International organization membership of the United States") and plays a leading role in global political, cultural, economic, and military affairs.

## Etymology

Further information: [Names of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Names_of_the_United_States "Names of the United States"), [Demonyms for the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demonyms_for_the_United_States "Demonyms for the United States"), [United Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Colonies "United Colonies"), and [Naming of the Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naming_of_the_Americas "Naming of the Americas")

Documented use of the phrase "United States of America" dates back to January 2, 1776. On that day, [Stephen Moylan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stephen_Moylan "Stephen Moylan"), a [Continental Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Army "Continental Army") aide to General [George Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington"), wrote a letter to [Joseph Reed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joseph_Reed_\(politician\) "Joseph Reed (politician)"), Washington's [aide-de-camp](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aide-de-camp "Aide-de-camp"), seeking to go "with full and ample powers from the United States of America to Spain" to seek assistance in the [Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War") effort.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLear-20132_32-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-DeLear-20132-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first known public usage is an [anonymous essay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anonymous_work "Anonymous work") published in the [Williamsburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia "Williamsburg, Virginia") newspaper *[The Virginia Gazette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Virginia_Gazette "The Virginia Gazette")* on April 6, 1776.<sup id="cite_ref-DeLear-20132_32-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-DeLear-20132-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Sometime on or after June 11, 1776, [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") wrote "United States of America" in a rough draft of the [Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence"),<sup id="cite_ref-DeLear-20132_32-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-DeLear-20132-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which was adopted by the [Second Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress") on July 4, 1776.<sup id="cite_ref-Davis72_34-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Davis72-34"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The term "United States" and its initialism "U.S.", used as nouns or as adjectives in English, are common short names for the country. The initialism "USA", a noun, is also common.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "United States" and "U.S." are the established terms throughout the [U.S. federal government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States"), with prescribed rules.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>l<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "The States" is an established colloquial shortening of the name, used particularly from abroad;<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "stateside" is the corresponding adjective or adverb.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

"America" is the feminine form of the first word of *Americus Vesputius*, the Latinized name of Italian explorer [Amerigo Vespucci](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amerigo_Vespucci "Amerigo Vespucci") (1454–1512); it was first used as a place name by the German cartographers [Martin Waldseemüller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Waldseem%C3%BCller "Martin Waldseemüller") and [Matthias Ringmann](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matthias_Ringmann "Matthias Ringmann") in 1507.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>m<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Vespucci first proposed that the [West Indies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Indies "West Indies") discovered by [Christopher Columbus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Columbus "Christopher Columbus") in 1492 were part of a previously unknown landmass and not among the Indies at the eastern limit of Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-locnamingofamerica_44-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-locnamingofamerica-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In English, [the term "America"](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas_\(terminology\) "Americas (terminology)") rarely refers to topics unrelated to the United States, despite the usage of "the [Americas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americas "Americas")" to describe the totality of [North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America") and [South America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_America "South America").<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## History

Main article: [History of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States "History of the United States")

For a topical guide, see [Outline of the history of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Outline_of_the_history_of_the_United_States "Outline of the history of the United States").

### Indigenous peoples

Main articles: [History of Native Americans in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "History of Native Americans in the United States") and [Pre-Columbian era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era "Pre-Columbian era")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Extreme_Makeover%2C_Mesa_Verde_Edition_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Extreme_Makeover%2C_Mesa_Verde_Edition_-_panoramio.jpg)

[Cliff Palace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cliff_Palace "Cliff Palace"), a settlement of [ancestors of](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans "Ancestral Puebloans") the [Native American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States "Native Americans in the United States") [Pueblo peoples](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pueblo_peoples "Pueblo peoples") in present-day [Montezuma County, Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Montezuma_County,_Colorado "Montezuma County, Colorado"), built between c. 1200 and 1275<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [first inhabitants of North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paleo-Indians "Paleo-Indians") migrated from [Siberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siberia "Siberia") over 12,000 years ago, either across the [Bering land bridge](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bering_land_bridge "Bering land bridge") or along the [now-submerged Ice Age coastline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_migration_\(Americas\) "Coastal migration (Americas)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEErlandsonRickVellanoweth200819_47-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEErlandsonRickVellanoweth200819-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESavage201155–58_48-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTESavage201155%E2%80%9358-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Clovis culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clovis_culture "Clovis culture"), which appeared around 11,000 BC, is believed to be the first widespread culture in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWatersStafford20071122–1126_49-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWatersStafford20071122%E2%80%931126-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFlannery2015173–185_50-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFlannery2015173%E2%80%93185-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Over time, indigenous North American cultures grew increasingly sophisticated, and some, such as the [Mississippian culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippian_culture "Mississippian culture"), developed [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_Agricultural_Complex "Eastern Agricultural Complex"), [architecture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeastern_Ceremonial_Complex "Southeastern Ceremonial Complex"), and [complex societies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Complex_societies "Complex societies").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELockard2010315_51-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTELockard2010315-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the [post-archaic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Native_Americans_in_the_United_States#Post-Archaic_stage "History of Native Americans in the United States"), the Mississippian cultures were located in the [midwestern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States"), [eastern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eastern_United_States "Eastern United States"), and [southern](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_United_States "Southern United States") regions, and the [Algonquian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algonquian_peoples "Algonquian peoples") in the [Great Lakes region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes_region "Great Lakes region") and along the [Eastern Seaboard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States"), while the [Hohokam culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hohokam_culture "Hohokam culture") and [Ancestral Puebloans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ancestral_Puebloans "Ancestral Puebloans") inhabited the [southwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Southwest "American Southwest").<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Native population estimates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Population_history_of_the_Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas "Population history of the Indigenous peoples of the Americas") of what is now the United States before the arrival of European immigrants range from around 500,000<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThornton199834_53-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThornton199834-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540_54-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> to nearly 10 million.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540_54-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPerdueGreen200540-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHainesHainesSteckel200012_55-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHainesHainesSteckel200012-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### European exploration, colonization and conflict (1513–1765)

Main articles: [Colonial history of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Colonial history of the United States") and [Colonial American military history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_American_military_history "Colonial American military history")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg/330px-Nouvelle-France_map-en.svg.png)

The [colonial possessions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Colonial history of the United States") of [Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") (the Thirteen Colonies in pink and others in purple), [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_France "New France") (in blue), and [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Spain "Kingdom of Spain") (in orange) in North America, 1750

[Christopher Columbus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christopher_Columbus "Christopher Columbus") began exploring the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean") for Spain in 1492, leading to [Spanish-speaking settlements and missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Empire "Spanish Empire") from [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico") and [Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida") to [New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico "Santa Fe de Nuevo México") and [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alta_California "Alta California"). The first Spanish colony in what is now the continental United States was [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida"), chartered in 1513.<sup id="cite_ref-Galloway2006_56-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Galloway2006-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hudson2018_57-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Hudson2018-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After several settlements failed there due to hunger and disease, Spain's first permanent town, [Saint Augustine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Florida "Saint Augustine, Florida"), was founded in 1565.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> France established its own settlements in [French Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Florida "French Florida") in 1562, but they were either abandoned (Charlesfort, 1578) or destroyed by Spanish raids ([Fort Caroline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Caroline "Fort Caroline"), 1565); [permanent French settlements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_France "New France") would be founded much later along the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes") ([Fort Detroit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fort_Pontchartrain_du_D%C3%A9troit "Fort Pontchartrain du Détroit"), 1701), the [Mississippi River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River") (Saint Louis, 1764) and especially the [Gulf of Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico "Gulf of Mexico") ([New Orleans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans "New Orleans"), 1718).<sup id="cite_ref-Petto20072_61-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Petto20072-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Early European colonies also included the thriving Dutch colony of [New Nederland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Nederland "New Nederland") (settled 1626, present-day New York) and the small Swedish colony of [New Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Sweden "New Sweden") (settled 1638 in what is now Delaware). [British colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_colonization_of_the_Americas "British colonization of the Americas") of the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") began with the [Virginia Colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia "Colony of Virginia") (1607) and the [Plymouth Colony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plymouth_Colony "Plymouth Colony") (Massachusetts, 1620).<sup id="cite_ref-Jr.Selby20182_62-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Jr.Selby20182-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BellahSullivan20062_63-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-BellahSullivan20062-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Mayflower Compact](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mayflower_Compact "Mayflower Compact") in Massachusetts and the [Fundamental Orders of Connecticut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fundamental_Orders_of_Connecticut "Fundamental Orders of Connecticut") established precedents for representative [self-governance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-governance "Self-governance") and [constitutionalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutionalism "Constitutionalism") that would develop throughout the American colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-Remini2–32_64-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Remini2%E2%80%9332-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Johnson26–302_65-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Johnson26%E2%80%93302-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> While European settlers in what is now the United States experienced conflicts with Native Americans, they also engaged in trade, exchanging European tools for food and animal pelts.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>n<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Relations ranged from close cooperation to warfare and massacres. The colonial authorities often pursued policies that forced Native Americans to adopt European lifestyles, including conversion to Christianity.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Along the eastern seaboard, settlers [trafficked African slaves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Slavery in the colonial history of the United States") through the [Atlantic slave trade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade "Atlantic slave trade").<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The original [Thirteen Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies "Thirteen Colonies")<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>o<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> that would later found the United States were administered as possessions of [Great Britain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Empire "British Empire"),<sup id="cite_ref-BilhartzElliott20072_75-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-BilhartzElliott20072-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and had [local governments with elections open to most white male property owners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonial_government_in_the_Thirteen_Colonies "Colonial government in the Thirteen Colonies").<sup id="cite_ref-Wood19982_76-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Wood19982-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The colonial population grew rapidly from Maine to Georgia, eclipsing Native American populations;<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> by the 1770s, the natural increase of the population was such that only a small minority of Americans had been born overseas.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The colonies' distance from Britain allowed for the development of self-governance,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the [First Great Awakening](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Great_Awakening "First Great Awakening"), a series of [Christian revivals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_revival "Christian revival"), fueled colonial interest in [religious liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freedom_of_religion "Freedom of religion").<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### American Revolution and the early republic (1765–1800)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1776–1789)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1776%E2%80%931789\) "History of the United States (1776–1789)"), [History of the United States (1789–1815)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1789%E2%80%931815\) "History of the United States (1789–1815)"), and [American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution")

![See caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg/250px-Declaration_of_Independence_%281819%29%2C_by_John_Trumbull.jpg)

*[Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_Independence_\(painting\) "Declaration of Independence (painting)")*, a portrait by [John Trumbull](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Trumbull "John Trumbull") depicting the [Committee of Five](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Five "Committee of Five") presenting the draft of [the Declaration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence") to the [Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress") on June 28, 1776, in [Philadelphia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philadelphia "Philadelphia")

Following their victory in the French and Indian War, Britain began to assert greater control over local colonial affairs, resulting in [colonial political resistance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolution "American Revolution"); one of the primary colonial grievances was a denial of their [rights as Englishmen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rights_of_Englishmen "Rights of Englishmen"), particularly the right to [representation in the British government that taxed them](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/No_taxation_without_representation "No taxation without representation"). To demonstrate their dissatisfaction and resolve, the [First Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Continental_Congress "First Continental Congress") met in 1774 and passed the [Continental Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Association "Continental Association"), a colonial boycott of British goods that proved effective. The British attempt to then disarm the colonists resulted in the 1775 [Battles of Lexington and Concord](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battles_of_Lexington_and_Concord "Battles of Lexington and Concord"), igniting the [American Revolutionary War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War "American Revolutionary War"). At the [Second Continental Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress "Second Continental Congress"), the colonies appointed [George Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington "George Washington") commander-in-chief of the [Continental Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Continental_Army "Continental Army"), and created [a committee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Committee_of_Five "Committee of Five") that named [Thomas Jefferson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Jefferson "Thomas Jefferson") to draft the [Declaration of Independence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence "United States Declaration of Independence"). Two days after passing the [Lee Resolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lee_Resolution "Lee Resolution") to create an independent nation the Declaration was adopted on July 4, 1776.<sup id="cite_ref-YoungNash20112_82-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-YoungNash20112-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [political values of the American Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Enlightenment "American Enlightenment") included [liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Liberty "Liberty"), [inalienable individual rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_rights_and_legal_rights "Natural rights and legal rights"); and the [sovereignty of the people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Popular_sovereignty "Popular sovereignty");<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> supporting [republicanism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republicanism_in_the_United_States "Republicanism in the United States") and rejecting [monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monarchy "Monarchy"), [aristocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristocracy "Aristocracy"), and all hereditary political power; [civic virtue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civic_virtue "Civic virtue"); and vilification of [political corruption](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_corruption "Political corruption").<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Founding Fathers of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States "Founding Fathers of the United States"), who included Washington, Jefferson, [John Adams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Adams "John Adams"), [Benjamin Franklin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin "Benjamin Franklin"), [Alexander Hamilton](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Hamilton "Alexander Hamilton"), [John Jay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Jay "John Jay"), [James Madison](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Madison "James Madison"), [Thomas Paine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Paine "Thomas Paine"), and many others, were inspired by [Greco-Roman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greco-Roman_world "Greco-Roman world"), [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance"), and [Enlightenment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment "Age of Enlightenment") philosophies and ideas.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SEoP-2006_86-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-SEoP-2006-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [Articles of Confederation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Articles_of_Confederation "Articles of Confederation") [and Perpetual Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perpetual_Union "Perpetual Union") were ratified in 1781 and established a decentralized government that operated until 1789.<sup id="cite_ref-YoungNash20112_82-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-YoungNash20112-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After the British surrender at the [siege of Yorktown](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Yorktown "Siege of Yorktown") in 1781, American sovereignty was internationally recognized by the [Treaty of Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_\(1783\) "Treaty of Paris (1783)") (1783), through which the U.S. gained territory stretching west to the Mississippi River, north to present-day Canada, and south to [Spanish Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_Florida "Spanish Florida").<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Northwest Ordinance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwest_Ordinance "Northwest Ordinance") (1787) established the precedent by which the country's territory would expand with the [admission of new states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union "Admission to the Union"), rather than the expansion of existing states.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [U.S. Constitution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States") was drafted at the 1787 [Constitutional Convention](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitutional_Convention_\(United_States\) "Constitutional Convention (United States)") to overcome the limitations of the Articles. It went into effect in 1789, creating a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") governed by [three separate branches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Separation_of_powers "Separation of powers") that together ensured a system of [checks and balances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Checks_and_balances "Checks and balances").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoner2020524_89-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner2020524-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> George Washington [was elected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1788%E2%80%9389_United_States_presidential_election "1788–89 United States presidential election") the country's first president under the Constitution, and the [Bill of Rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Bill_of_Rights "United States Bill of Rights") was adopted in 1791 to allay skeptics' concerns about the power of the more centralized government.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014§_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages8-1-competing-visions-federalists-and-democratic-republicans_8.1]_90-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014%C2%A7_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages8-1-competing-visions-federalists-and-democratic-republicans_8.1]-90"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFoner2020538–540_91-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFoner2020538%E2%80%93540-91"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [His resignation as commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Washington%27s_resignation_as_commander-in-chief "George Washington's resignation as commander-in-chief") after the Revolutionary War and his later refusal to run for a third term as the country's first president established a precedent for the supremacy of civil authority in the United States and the [peaceful transfer of power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peaceful_transition_of_power "Peaceful transition of power").<sup id="cite_ref-BoyerJr.20072_92-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-BoyerJr.20072-92"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014§_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages8-1-competing-visions-federalists-and-democratic-republicans_8.3]_93-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014%C2%A7_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages8-1-competing-visions-federalists-and-democratic-republicans_8.3]-93"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Westward expansion and Civil War (1800–1865)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1815–1849)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1815%E2%80%931849\) "History of the United States (1815–1849)") and [History of the United States (1849–1865)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1849%E2%80%931865\) "History of the United States (1849–1865)")

![Historical territorial expansion of the United States](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png/330px-U.S._Territorial_Acquisitions.png)

[Territorial expansion of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States "Territorial evolution of the United States")

The [Louisiana Purchase](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase "Louisiana Purchase") of 1803 from France nearly doubled the territory of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Lingering issues with Britain remained](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_War_of_1812 "Origins of the War of 1812"), leading to the [War of 1812](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_of_1812 "War of 1812"), which was fought to a draw.<sup id="cite_ref-Wait19992_96-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Wait19992-96"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Spain ceded Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adams%E2%80%93On%C3%ADs_Treaty "Adams–Onís Treaty") and its Gulf Coast territory in 1819.<sup id="cite_ref-KloseJones19942_98-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-KloseJones19942-98"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the late 18th century, American settlers began to [expand westward](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territorial_evolution_of_the_United_States "Territorial evolution of the United States"), many with a sense of [manifest destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manifest_destiny "Manifest destiny").<sup id="cite_ref-MD20072_99-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-MD20072-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198841–46_100-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198841%E2%80%9346-100"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Missouri Compromise](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri_Compromise "Missouri Compromise") of 1820, which admitted [Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Missouri "Missouri") as a [slave state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") and [Maine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maine#Statehood "Maine") as a free state, attempted to balance the desire of northern states to prevent the expansion of slavery into new territories with that of southern states to extend it there. The compromise further prohibited slavery in all other lands of the Louisiana Purchase north of the [36°30′ parallel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parallel_36%C2%B030%E2%80%B2_north "Parallel 36°30′ north").<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> As Americans expanded further into land inhabited by Native Americans, the federal government often applied [policies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Indian_Policy "Federal Indian Policy") of [Indian removal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_removal "Indian removal") or [assimilation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cultural_assimilation_of_Native_Americans "Cultural assimilation of Native Americans").<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The most significant removal legislation in U.S. history was the [Indian Removal Act of 1830](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Removal_Act "Indian Removal Act"). It culminated in the [Trail of Tears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trail_of_Tears "Trail of Tears") (1830–1850), in which an estimated 60,000 Native Americans living east of the [Mississippi River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River "Mississippi River") were forcibly removed and displaced to lands far to the west, resulting in anywhere from 13,200 to 16,700 deaths.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198845_104-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson198845-104"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These and earlier organized displacements prompted a long series of [American Indian Wars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Indian_Wars "American Indian Wars") west of the Mississippi.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-105"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BillingtonRidge2001j2_106-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-BillingtonRidge2001j2-106"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Republic of Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_Texas "Republic of Texas") was [annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_annexation "Texas annexation") in 1845,<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison19992_107-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Morrison19992-107"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the 1846 [Oregon Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oregon_Treaty "Oregon Treaty") led to U.S. control of the present-day [American Northwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northwestern_United_States "Northwestern United States").<sup id="cite_ref-Kemp20102_108-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kemp20102-108"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Victory in the [Mexican–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War "Mexican–American War") resulted in the 1848 [Mexican Cession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_Cession "Mexican Cession") of California, Nevada, Utah, and much of present-day Colorado and the [American Southwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwestern_United_States "Southwestern United States").<sup id="cite_ref-MD20072_99-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-MD20072-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-McIlwraithMuller20012_109-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-McIlwraithMuller20012-109"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [California gold rush](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_gold_rush "California gold rush") of 1848–1849 spurred a huge migration of white settlers to the Pacific coast, leading to even more confrontations with Native populations. One of the most violent, the [California genocide](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_genocide "California genocide") of thousands of Native inhabitants, lasted into the early 1870s,<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-110"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> just as additional western territories and states were created.<sup id="cite_ref-Rawls1999_111-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Rawls1999-111"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![Division of the states during the American Civil War: Union, Confederacy, border states, and territories](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/US_map_1864_Civil_War_divisions.svg/330px-US_map_1864_Civil_War_divisions.svg.png)

Division of the states during the [American Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War"): 

  [Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_\(American_Civil_War\) "Union (American Civil War)")

  [Confederacy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America "Confederate States of America")

  [Border states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Border_states_\(American_Civil_War\) "Border states (American Civil War)")

  [Territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States")

During the colonial period, [slavery had been legal in the American colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slavery_in_the_colonial_history_of_the_United_States "Slavery in the colonial history of the United States"), especially in the agriculture-intensive [Southern Colonies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_Colonies "Southern Colonies") from Maryland to Georgia. The practice began to be significantly questioned during the American Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752–54Wright2022_112-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752%E2%80%9354Wright2022-112"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Spurred by an active [abolitionist movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_States "Abolitionism in the United States") that had reemerged in the 1830s, states in [the North](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_United_States "Northern United States") enacted anti-slavery laws.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752–54Rodriguez2015XXXIVWright2022_113-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe200752%E2%80%9354Rodriguez2015XXXIVWright2022-113"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> At the same time, support for slavery had strengthened in [Southern states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southern_United_States "Southern United States") with inventions such as the [cotton gin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cotton_gin "Cotton gin") (1793), which had long made the institution profitable for [Southern elites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Planter_class "Planter class").<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe2007478,_481–482,_587–588_116-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWalker_Howe2007478,_481%E2%80%93482,_587%E2%80%93588-116"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Throughout the 1850s, this [sectional conflict regarding slavery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slave_states_and_free_states "Slave states and free states") was further inflamed by legislation in Congress and decisions of the Supreme Court: The [Fugitive Slave Act of 1850](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fugitive_Slave_Act_of_1850 "Fugitive Slave Act of 1850") mandated the return of slaves taking refuge in non-slave states to their owners in the South. The [Kansas–Nebraska Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas%E2%80%93Nebraska_Act "Kansas–Nebraska Act") of 1854 effectively gutted the anti-slavery requirements of the Missouri Compromise.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-117"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Finally, in its [Dred Scott decision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dred_Scott_v._Sandford "Dred Scott v. Sandford") of 1857, the Supreme Court ruled against a slave brought into non-slave territory and declared the Missouri Compromise to be unconstitutional. These events exacerbated tensions between North and South that would [culminate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Origins_of_the_American_Civil_War "Origins of the American Civil War") in the [American Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Civil_War "American Civil War") (1861–1865).<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-118"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Woods_2012_pp._415–4392_119-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Woods_2012_pp._415%E2%80%934392-119"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Eleven slave states [seceded](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seceded "Seceded") and formed the [Confederate States of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America "Confederate States of America"), while the other states remained in [the Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_\(American_Civil_War\) "Union (American Civil War)").<sup id="cite_ref-Silkenat_2019_p._252_120-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Silkenat_2019_p._252-120"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988236_121-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988236-121"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> War broke out in April 1861 after the Confederates [bombarded Fort Sumter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Sumter "Battle of Fort Sumter").<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988273–274_123-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcPherson1988273%E2%80%93274-123"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After the January 1863 [Emancipation Proclamation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emancipation_Proclamation "Emancipation Proclamation"), many freed slaves joined the [Union army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Union_army "Union army").<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The war [began to turn in the Union's favor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turning_point_of_the_American_Civil_War "Turning point of the American Civil War") following the 1863 [Siege of Vicksburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Vicksburg "Siege of Vicksburg") and [Battle of Gettysburg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Gettysburg "Battle of Gettysburg"), and the Confederacy surrendered in 1865 after the Union's victory in the [Battle of Appomattox Court House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Appomattox_Court_House "Battle of Appomattox Court House").<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Reconstruction era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_era "Reconstruction era") followed the war. After [the assassination](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assassination_of_Abraham_Lincoln "Assassination of Abraham Lincoln") of President [Abraham Lincoln](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln "Abraham Lincoln"), [Reconstruction Amendments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reconstruction_Amendments "Reconstruction Amendments") were passed to [protect the rights of African Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement_\(1865%E2%80%931896\) "Civil rights movement (1865–1896)"). National infrastructure, including [transcontinental telegraph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_transcontinental_telegraph "First transcontinental telegraph") and [railroads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_transcontinental_railroad "First transcontinental railroad"), spurred growth in the [American frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_frontier "American frontier").<sup id="cite_ref-Black2011kj2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Black2011kj2-126"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Post–Civil War era (1865–1917)

Main article: [History of the United States (1865–1917)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1865%E2%80%931917\) "History of the United States (1865–1917)")

<video id="mwe_player_1_placeholder" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Emigrants_%28i.e._immigrants%29_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm/250px--Emigrants_%28i.e._immigrants%29_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm.jpg" preload="none" data-mw-tmh="" class="mw-file-element" width="250" height="188" data-durationhint="147" data-mwtitle="Emigrants_(i.e._immigrants)_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons" resource="/wiki/File:Emigrants_(i.e._immigrants)_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm" playsinline="" disabled="disabled" tabindex="-1" style="aspect-ratio: 250 / 188;"></video>_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm "Play video")Duration: 2 minutes and 27 seconds.2:27_landing_at_Ellis_Island_-.webm)

An [Edison Studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edison_Studios "Edison Studios") film showing immigrants arriving at [Ellis Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ellis_Island "Ellis Island") in [New York Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Harbor "New York Harbor"), a major point of entry for European [immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Immigration_to_the_United_States "Immigration to the United States") in the late 19th and early 20th centuries<sup id="cite_ref-PriceBenton-Short2008_127-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-PriceBenton-Short2008-127"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

From 1865 through 1917, an unprecedented stream of immigrants arrived in the United States, including 24.4 million from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Most came through the [port of New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_New_York_and_New_Jersey "Port of New York and New Jersey"), and New York City and other large cities on the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") became home to large [Jewish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_the_United_States "History of the Jews in the United States"), [Irish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irish_Americans "Irish Americans"), and [Italian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_Americans "Italian Americans") populations, while many [Germans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Americans "German Americans") and Central Europeans moved to the [Midwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States"). At the same time, about one million [French Canadians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French-Canadian_Americans "French-Canadian Americans") migrated from [Quebec](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quebec "Quebec") to [New England](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England "New England").<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the [Great Migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Migration_\(African_American\) "Great Migration (African American)"), millions of African Americans [left the rural South](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_economy "Jim Crow economy") for urban areas in the North.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Alaska was purchased](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Purchase "Alaska Purchase") from [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Empire "Russian Empire") in 1867.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [Compromise of 1877](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compromise_of_1877 "Compromise of 1877") effectively ended Reconstruction and [white supremacists took local control of Southern politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redeemers "Redeemers").<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> African Americans endured a period of heightened, overt racism following Reconstruction, a time often called the [nadir of American race relations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nadir_of_American_race_relations "Nadir of American race relations").<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA2_135-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-ReferenceA2-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> A series of Supreme Court decisions, including *[Plessy v. Ferguson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plessy_v._Ferguson "Plessy v. Ferguson")*, emptied the Fourteenth and Fifteenth Amendments of their force, allowing [Jim Crow laws](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_Crow_laws "Jim Crow laws") in the South to remain unchecked, [sundown towns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sundown_town "Sundown town") in the Midwest, and [segregation in communities across the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Racial_segregation_in_the_United_States "Racial segregation in the United States"), which would be reinforced by the policy of [redlining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Redlining "Redlining") later adopted by the federal [Home Owners' Loan Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Owners%27_Loan_Corporation "Home Owners' Loan Corporation").<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[An explosion of technological advancement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Industrial_Revolution "Second Industrial Revolution") accompanied by the exploitation of cheap immigrant labor<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> led to [rapid economic expansion during the late 19th and early 20th centuries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gilded_Age "Gilded Age"), allowing the United States to outpace the economies of England, France, and Germany combined.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This fostered the amassing of power by [a few prominent industrialists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robber_baron_\(industrialist\) "Robber baron (industrialist)"), largely by their formation of [trusts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trust_\(business\) "Trust (business)") and [monopolies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monopoly "Monopoly") to prevent competition.<sup id="cite_ref-Atlantic2_141-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Atlantic2-141"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Tycoons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tycoon "Tycoon") led the nation's expansion in the [railroad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_rail_transportation_in_the_United_States "History of rail transportation in the United States"), [petroleum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_petroleum_industry_in_the_United_States "History of the petroleum industry in the United States"), and [steel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_steel_industry_\(1850%E2%80%931970\) "History of the steel industry (1850–1970)") industries. The United States emerged as a pioneer of the [automotive industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States "Automotive industry in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> These changes were accompanied by significant increases in [economic inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_inequality "Economic inequality"), [slum conditions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/How_the_Other_Half_Lives "How the Other Half Lives"), and [social unrest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_incidents_of_civil_unrest_in_the_United_States "List of incidents of civil unrest in the United States"), creating the environment for [labor unions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labor_history_of_the_United_States "Labor history of the United States") and [socialist movements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_socialist_movement_in_the_United_States "History of the socialist movement in the United States") to begin to flourish.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fraser2_145-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Fraser2-145"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This period eventually ended with the advent of the [Progressive Era](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Progressive_Era "Progressive Era"), which was characterized by significant reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-Aldrich2_146-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Aldrich2-146"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Pro-American elements in Hawaii [overthrew the Hawaiian monarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overthrow_of_the_Hawaiian_Kingdom "Overthrow of the Hawaiian Kingdom"); the islands [were annexed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Newlands_Resolution "Newlands Resolution") in 1898. That same year, [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), [the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Philippines "The Philippines"), and [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam") were ceded to the U.S. by Spain after the latter's defeat in the [Spanish–American War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War "Spanish–American War"). (The Philippines was granted full independence from the U.S. on July 4, 1946, following World War II. Puerto Rico and Guam have remained U.S. territories.)<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa") was acquired by the United States in 1900 after the [Second Samoan Civil War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Second_Samoan_Civil_War "Second Samoan Civil War").<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands") were purchased from [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark "Denmark") in 1917.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Rise as a superpower (1917–1945)

Main article: [History of the United States (1917–1945)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1917%E2%80%931945\) "History of the United States (1917–1945)")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Trinity_shot_color_%284x3_cropped%29.jpg/250px-Trinity_shot_color_%284x3_cropped%29.jpg)

The 1945 [Trinity test](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trinity_\(nuclear_test\) "Trinity (nuclear test)"), during which the U.S. conducted the first-ever detonation of a [nuclear weapon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapon "Nuclear weapon")
