The United States [entered World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I "American entry into World War I") alongside the [Allies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") in 1917 helping to turn the tide against the [Central Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Powers "Central Powers").<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-151"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 1920, [a constitutional amendment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nineteenth_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Nineteenth Amendment to the United States Constitution") granted nationwide [women's suffrage](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_suffrage_in_the_United_States "Women's suffrage in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the 1920s and 1930s, radio for [mass communication](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_communication "Mass communication") and early television transformed communications nationwide.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013410–411_153-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013410%E2%80%93411-153"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Wall Street Crash of 1929](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929 "Wall Street Crash of 1929") triggered the [Great Depression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Depression_in_the_United_States "Great Depression in the United States"), which President [Franklin D. Roosevelt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt "Franklin D. Roosevelt") responded to with the [New Deal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Deal "New Deal"), a series of [sweeping programs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alphabet_agencies "Alphabet agencies") and [public works projects](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Works_Progress_Administration "Works Progress Administration") combined with financial reforms and [regulations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regulatory_economics "Regulatory economics"). All were intended to protect against future economic depressions.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[Initially neutral](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_non-interventionism_before_entering_World_War_II "United States non-interventionism before entering World War II") during [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_history_of_the_United_States_during_World_War_II "Military history of the United States during World War II"), the U.S. began [supplying war materiel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lend-Lease "Lend-Lease") to the [Allies of World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II "Allies of World War II") in March 1941 and [entered the war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_II "American entry into World War II") in December after the [Empire of Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire_of_Japan "Empire of Japan")'s [attack on Pearl Harbor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor "Attack on Pearl Harbor").<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pearl_Harbor2_157-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Pearl_Harbor2-157"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. [developed the first nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan_Project "Manhattan Project") and [used them against the Japanese cities of Hiroshima and Nagasaki](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki "Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki") in August 1945, ending the war.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States was one of the "[Four Policemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Four_Policemen "Four Policemen")" who met to plan the [post-war world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II"), alongside the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom"), [Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soviet_Union "Soviet Union"), and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republic_of_China_\(1912%E2%80%931949\) "Republic of China (1912–1949)").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHoopesBrinkley1997100_160-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHoopesBrinkley1997100-160"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGaddis197225_161-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGaddis197225-161"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. emerged relatively unscathed from the war, with even greater [economic power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economic_power "Economic power") and [international political influence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sphere_of_influence "Sphere of influence").<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Cold War (1945–1991)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1945–1964)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1945%E2%80%931964\) "History of the United States (1945–1964)"), [History of the United States (1964–1980)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1964%E2%80%931980\) "History of the United States (1964–1980)"), and [History of the United States (1980–1991)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1980%E2%80%931991\) "History of the United States (1980–1991)")

![Mikhail Gorbachev and Ronald Reagan sign the Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty at the White House in 1987. Gorbachev was the final leader of the Soviet Union before its dissolution in 1991.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg/250px-Reagan_and_Gorbachev_signing.jpg)

[Mikhail Gorbachev](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev "Mikhail Gorbachev") and [Ronald Reagan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Reagan "Ronald Reagan") sign the [Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Intermediate-Range_Nuclear_Forces_Treaty "Intermediate-Range Nuclear Forces Treaty") at the [White House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House") in 1987.

The end of World War II in 1945 left the U.S. and the Soviet Union as superpowers, each with its own political, military, and economic sphere of influence. Geopolitical tensions between the two superpowers soon led to the [Cold War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cold_War "Cold War").<sup id="cite_ref-Blakemore-20192_163-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Blakemore-20192-163"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. utilized the policy of [containment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Containment "Containment") to limit the USSR's sphere of influence, engaged in [regime change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_involvement_in_regime_change#1945%E2%80%931991:_Cold_War "United States involvement in regime change") against governments perceived to be aligned with Moscow, and prevailed in the [Space Race](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Race "Space Race"), which culminated with the [first crewed Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proxy2_167-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Proxy2-167"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Domestically, the U.S. [experienced economic growth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post%E2%80%93World_War_II_economic_expansion "Post–World War II economic expansion"), [urbanization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Urbanization_in_the_United_States "Urbanization in the United States"), and [population growth following World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mid-20th_century_baby_boom "Mid-20th century baby boom").<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013305–308_168-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWinchester2013305%E2%80%93308-168"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [civil rights movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights_movement "Civil rights movement") emerged, with [Martin Luther King Jr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Jr. "Martin Luther King Jr.") becoming a prominent leader in the early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Great Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Society "Great Society") plan of President [Lyndon B. Johnson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson "Lyndon B. Johnson")'s administration resulted in groundbreaking and broad-reaching laws, policies and a constitutional amendment to counteract some of the worst effects of lingering [institutional racism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Institutional_racism "Institutional racism").<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [counterculture movement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Counterculture_of_the_1960s "Counterculture of the 1960s") in the U.S. brought significant social changes, including the liberalization of attitudes toward [recreational drug use](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recreational_drug_use "Recreational drug use") and [sexuality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sexual_revolution "Sexual revolution").<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It also encouraged [open defiance of the military draft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Draft_evasion_in_the_Vietnam_War "Draft evasion in the Vietnam War") (leading to the [end of conscription](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conscription_in_the_United_States "Conscription in the United States") in 1973) and [wide opposition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opposition_to_United_States_involvement_in_the_Vietnam_War "Opposition to United States involvement in the Vietnam War") to [U.S. intervention in Vietnam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_in_the_Vietnam_War "United States in the Vietnam War") (with the U.S. totally withdrawing in 1975).<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [A societal shift in the roles of women](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women%27s_liberation_movement "Women's liberation movement") was significantly responsible for the large increase in female paid labor participation during the 1970s, and by 1985 the majority of American women aged 16 and older were employed.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-174"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [fall of communism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Revolutions_of_1989 "Revolutions of 1989") and the [collapse of the Soviet Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Soviet_Union "Dissolution of the Soviet Union") from 1989 to 1991 marked the end of the Cold War and [left the United States as the world's sole superpower](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superpower#After_the_Cold_War "Superpower").<sup id="cite_ref-Gaidar2_175-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Gaidar2-175"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-176"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-177"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-178"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This cemented the United States' global influence, reinforcing the concept of the "[American Century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Century "American Century")" as it dominated international politics, economics, and military affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-179"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-180"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Contemporary (1991–present)

Main articles: [History of the United States (1991–2016)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(1991%E2%80%932016\) "History of the United States (1991–2016)") and [History of the United States (2016–present)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_\(2016%E2%80%93present\) "History of the United States (2016–present)")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Explosion_following_the_plane_impact_into_the_South_Tower_%28WTC_2%29_-_B6019~11.jpg/250px-Explosion_following_the_plane_impact_into_the_South_Tower_%28WTC_2%29_-_B6019~11.jpg)

The [Twin Towers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Trade_Center_\(1973%E2%80%932001\) "World Trade Center (1973–2001)") in New York City during the [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks") in 2001

The 1990s saw the [longest recorded economic expansion in American history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990s_United_States_boom "1990s United States boom"), a dramatic [decline in U.S. crime rates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_in_the_United_States#Crime_over_time "Crime in the United States"), and [advances in technology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_and_industrial_history_of_the_United_States#Computers_and_information_networks "Technological and industrial history of the United States"). Throughout this decade, technological innovations such as the [World Wide Web](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Wide_Web "World Wide Web"), the evolution of the [Pentium microprocessor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentium_\(original\) "Pentium (original)") in accordance with [Moore's law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moore%27s_law "Moore's law"), rechargeable [lithium-ion batteries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery "Lithium-ion battery"), the first [gene therapy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_therapy "Gene therapy") trial, and [cloning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cloning "Cloning") either emerged in the U.S. or were improved upon there. The [Human Genome Project](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Human_Genome_Project "Human Genome Project") was formally launched in 1990, while [Nasdaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasdaq "Nasdaq") became the first stock market in the United States to trade online in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-181"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In the [Gulf War](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_War "Gulf War") of 1991, an [American-led international coalition of states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coalition_of_the_Gulf_War "Coalition of the Gulf War") expelled an [Iraqi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ba%27athist_Iraq "Ba'athist Iraq") invasion force that had occupied neighboring [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait").<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-182"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [September 11 attacks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/September_11_attacks "September 11 attacks") on the United States in 2001 by the [pan-Islamist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Islamism "Pan-Islamism") militant organization [al-Qaeda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Qaeda "Al-Qaeda") led to the [war on terror](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_on_terror "War on terror"), and subsequent [military interventions in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_\(2001%E2%80%932021\) "War in Afghanistan (2001–2021)") and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq_War "Iraq War").<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-183"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-184"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [U.S. housing bubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000s_United_States_housing_bubble "2000s United States housing bubble") culminated in 2007 with the [Great Recession](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Recession "Great Recession"), the largest economic contraction since the Great Depression.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-185"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Coming to a head in the 2010s, [political polarization in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_polarization_in_the_United_States "Political polarization in the United States") increased between liberal and conservative factions.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-186"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-187"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-188"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> This polarization was capitalized upon in the [January 2021 Capitol attack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack "January 6 United States Capitol attack"),<sup id="cite_ref-Kleinfeld-2023_189-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kleinfeld-2023-189"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>174<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> when a mob of insurrectionists<sup id="cite_ref-Pape-2022_190-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Pape-2022-190"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>175<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> entered the [U.S. Capitol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol "United States Capitol") and sought to prevent the peaceful transfer of power<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-191"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>176<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> in an [attempted self-coup d'état](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Self-coup#Notable_events_described_as_attempted_self-coups "Self-coup").<sup id="cite_ref-Multiple_Sources_192-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Multiple_Sources-192"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>177<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [2021 Taliban offensive](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2021_Taliban_offensive "2021 Taliban offensive") (May–August) ended the [War in Afghanistan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_\(2001%E2%80%932021\) "War in Afghanistan (2001–2021)") one year after the [U.S. signed a peace agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Taliban_deal "United States–Taliban deal") with the Taliban.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT_taliban_strategy_193-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NYT_taliban_strategy-193"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>178<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Geography

Main article: [Geography of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_of_the_United_States "Geography of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Uspaintedrelief.png/250px-Uspaintedrelief.png)

A [topographic map](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topographic_map "Topographic map") of the United States

The United States is the world's [third-largest country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area "List of countries and dependencies by area") by total area behind Russia and Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-largestcountry_15-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-largestcountry-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>c<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA-2018_194-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CIA-2018-194"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CIA_Factbook_Area_195-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CIA_Factbook_Area-195"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>180<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 48 [contiguous states and the District of Columbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contiguous_United_States "Contiguous United States") occupy a combined area of 3,119,885 square miles (8,080,470 km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-CensusGov2010HTML_14-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CensusGov2010HTML-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-196"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>181<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-urlState_Area_Measurements_and_Internal_Point_Coordinates—Geography—U.S._Census_Bureau_197-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-urlState_Area_Measurements_and_Internal_Point_Coordinates%E2%80%94Geography%E2%80%94U.S._Census_Bureau-197"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>182<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [The coastal plain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Plain "Atlantic Plain") of the [Atlantic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") seaboard gives way to inland forests and rolling hills in the [Piedmont](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piedmont_\(United_States\) "Piedmont (United States)") plateau region.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-198"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>183<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [Appalachian Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains "Appalachian Mountains") and the [Adirondack](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adirondack_Mountains "Adirondack Mountains") massif separate the [East Coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States "East Coast of the United States") from the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes") and the grasslands of [the Midwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midwestern_United_States "Midwestern United States").<sup id="cite_ref-NAU_199-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NAU-199"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Mississippi River System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mississippi_River_System "Mississippi River System"), the world's [fourth-longest river system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_rivers_by_length "List of rivers by length"), runs predominantly north–south through the heart of the country. The flat and fertile [prairie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prairie "Prairie") of the [Great Plains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Plains "Great Plains") stretches to the west, interrupted by [a highland region](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Interior_Highlands "U.S. Interior Highlands") in the southeast.<sup id="cite_ref-NAU_199-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NAU-199"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>184<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Grand_Canyon_%2852931490880%29.jpg/250px-Grand_Canyon_%2852931490880%29.jpg)

The [Grand Canyon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Canyon "Grand Canyon") in Arizona

The [Rocky Mountains](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rocky_Mountains "Rocky Mountains"), west of the Great Plains, extend north to south across the country, peaking at over 14,000 feet (4,300 m) in [Colorado](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colorado "Colorado").<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-200"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>185<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Farther west are the rocky [Great Basin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Basin "Great Basin") and [Chihuahua](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chihuahuan_Desert "Chihuahuan Desert"), [Sonoran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sonoran_Desert "Sonoran Desert"), and [Mojave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mojave_Desert "Mojave Desert") deserts.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-201"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>186<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the northwest corner of [Arizona](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arizona "Arizona"), carved by the [Colorado River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colorado_River "Colorado River") over millions of years, is the [Grand Canyon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Canyon "Grand Canyon"), a steep-sided canyon and popular tourist destination known for its overwhelming visual size and intricate, colorful landscape.

The [Sierra Nevada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sierra_Nevada "Sierra Nevada") and [Cascade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cascade_Range "Cascade Range") mountain ranges run close to the [Pacific coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Coast_of_the_United_States "West Coast of the United States"). The [lowest and highest points in the contiguous United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_points_of_the_United_States "Extreme points of the United States") are in the State of California,<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-202"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>187<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> about 84 miles (135 km) apart.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-203"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>188<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> At an elevation of 20,310 feet (6,190.5 m), Alaska's [Denali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denali "Denali") is the highest peak in the country and continent.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-204"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>189<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Active [volcanoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_volcanoes_in_the_United_States "List of volcanoes in the United States") are common throughout Alaska's [Alexander](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Archipelago "Alexander Archipelago") and [Aleutian Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleutian_Islands "Aleutian Islands"), and Hawaii consists of volcanic islands. The [supervolcano](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervolcano "Supervolcano") underlying [Yellowstone National Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellowstone_National_Park "Yellowstone National Park") in the Rocky Mountains, the [Yellowstone Caldera](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yellowstone_Caldera "Yellowstone Caldera"), is the continent's largest volcanic feature.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-205"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>190<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2021, the United States had 8% of global permanent meadows and pastures and 10% of cropland.<sup id="cite_ref-Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_of_the_United_Nations-2023_206-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Food_and_Agriculture_Organization_of_the_United_Nations-2023-206"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>191<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Climate

Main article: [Climate of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_of_the_United_States "Climate of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_US_50.png/250px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_US_50.png)

The [Köppen climate types](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification "Köppen climate classification") of the United States

With its large size and geographic variety, the United States includes most climate types. East of the [100th meridian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/100th_meridian_west "100th meridian west"), the climate ranges from [humid continental](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_continental_climate "Humid continental climate") in the north to [humid subtropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Humid_subtropical_climate "Humid subtropical climate") in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>192<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The western Great Plains are [semi-arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Semi-arid_climate "Semi-arid climate").<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>193<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Many mountainous areas of the American West have an [alpine climate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alpine_climate "Alpine climate"). The climate is [arid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Desert_climate "Desert climate") in the Southwest, [Mediterranean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_climate "Mediterranean climate") in [coastal California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_California "Coastal California"), and [oceanic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oceanic_climate "Oceanic climate") in coastal [Oregon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oregon "Oregon"), [Washington](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_\(state\) "Washington (state)"), and southern [Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska "Alaska"). Most of Alaska is [subarctic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Subarctic_climate "Subarctic climate") or [polar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polar_climate "Polar climate"). [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii"), the [southern tip of Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Florida "South Florida") and U.S. territories in the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean") and [Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") are [tropical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tropical_climate "Tropical climate").<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>194<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States receives more high-impact [extreme weather](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme_weather "Extreme weather") incidents than any other country.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-210"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>195<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>196<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> States bordering the [Gulf of Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico "Gulf of Mexico") are prone to hurricanes, and most of the world's tornadoes [occur in the country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tornadoes_in_the_United_States "Tornadoes in the United States"), mainly in [Tornado Alley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tornado_Alley "Tornado Alley").<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-212"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>197<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Extreme weather became more frequent in the U.S. in the 21st century, with three times the number of reported [heat waves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Heat_waves "Heat waves") as in the 1960s. In the [American Southwest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southwestern_United_States "Southwestern United States"), droughts became more persistent and more severe.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-213"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>198<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The regions considered as the most attractive to the population are the most vulnerable.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-214"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>199<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Biodiversity and conservation

Main articles: [Fauna of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fauna_of_the_United_States "Fauna of the United States") and [Flora of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flora_of_the_United_States "Flora of the United States")

![A bald eagle](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Bald_eagle_about_to_fly_in_Alaska_%282016%29.jpg/250px-Bald_eagle_about_to_fly_in_Alaska_%282016%29.jpg)

The [bald eagle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bald_eagle "Bald eagle"), the [national emblem of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bald_eagle#National_symbol_of_the_United_States "Bald eagle") since 1782 and officially declared the national bird in 2024<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-215"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>200<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The U.S. is one of 17 [megadiverse countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Megadiverse_countries "Megadiverse countries") containing large numbers of [endemic species](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_endangered_animals_of_North_America "List of endangered animals of North America"): about 17,000 species of [vascular plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vascular_plant "Vascular plant") occur in the contiguous United States and Alaska, and over 1,800 species of [flowering plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowering_plant "Flowering plant") are found in Hawaii, few of which occur on the mainland.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-216"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>201<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is home to 428 [mammal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mammal "Mammal") species, 784 birds, 311 reptiles, 295 [amphibians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amphibian "Amphibian"),<sup id="cite_ref-Current_Results_#_of_native_species_in_the_US_217-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Current_Results_#_of_native_species_in_the_US-217"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>202<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and around 91,000 insect species.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-218"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>203<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

There are [63 national parks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_national_parks_of_the_United_States "List of national parks of the United States"), and [hundreds of other federally managed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_lands "Federal lands") parks, forests, and [wilderness areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System "National Wilderness Preservation System"), managed by the [National Park Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Park_Service "National Park Service") and other agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-219"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>204<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> About 28% of the country's land is publicly owned and federally managed,<sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_Federal_Land_220-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NYTimes_Federal_Land-220"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>205<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> primarily in the [Western States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Western_United_States "Western United States").<sup id="cite_ref-AKLeg_CRS_Federal_Land_221-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-AKLeg_CRS_Federal_Land-221"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Most of this land is protected](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Protected_areas_of_the_United_States "Protected areas of the United States"), though some is leased for commercial use, and less than one percent is used for military purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Federal_Land_Ownership_222-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Federal_Land_Ownership-222"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fed_Land_Uses_223-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Fed_Land_Uses-223"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[Environmental issues in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_issues_in_the_United_States "Environmental issues in the United States") include debates on [non-renewable resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-renewable_resource "Non-renewable resource") and [nuclear energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_debate "Nuclear power debate"), [air and water pollution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pollution_prevention_in_the_US "Pollution prevention in the US"), [biodiversity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biodiversity "Biodiversity"), logging and [deforestation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deforestation_in_the_United_States "Deforestation in the United States"),<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-224"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-225"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [climate change](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_United_States "Climate change in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-226"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-227"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [U.S. Environmental Protection Agency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency "United States Environmental Protection Agency") (EPA) is the federal agency charged with [addressing most environmental-related issues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_policy_of_the_United_States "Environmental policy of the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-Collin2006_228-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Collin2006-228"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>213<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [idea of wilderness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Wilderness_Preservation_System "National Wilderness Preservation System") has shaped the management of public lands since 1964, with the [Wilderness Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilderness_Act "Wilderness Act").<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-229"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>214<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Endangered Species Act of 1973](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Endangered_Species_Act_of_1973 "Endangered Species Act of 1973") provides a way to protect threatened and endangered species and their habitats. The [United States Fish and Wildlife Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Fish_and_Wildlife_Service "United States Fish and Wildlife Service") implements and enforces the Act.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_230-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Office-230"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>215<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2024, the U.S. ranked 35th among 180 countries in the [Environmental Performance Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index "Environmental Performance Index").<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-231"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>216<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Government and politics

Main article: [Politics of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics_of_the_United_States "Politics of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/US_Capitol_west_side.JPG/250px-US_Capitol_west_side.JPG)

The [U.S. Capitol Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Capitol "United States Capitol"), the seat of legislative government, is home to both chambers of the [U.S. Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Congress "U.S. Congress"): the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") and the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives").

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/White_House_lawn_%28long_tightly_cropped%29.jpg/250px-White_House_lawn_%28long_tightly_cropped%29.jpg)

The [White House](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White_House "White House"), the residence and workplace of the U.S. president and the offices of [the presidential staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Office_of_the_President_of_the_United_States "Executive Office of the President of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Panorama_of_United_States_Supreme_Court_Building_at_Dusk.jpg/250px-Panorama_of_United_States_Supreme_Court_Building_at_Dusk.jpg)

The [Supreme Court Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court_Building "United States Supreme Court Building"), which houses the [nation's highest court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States "Supreme Court of the United States")

The United States is a [federal republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_republic "Federal republic") of 50 [states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state"), and a federal capital district, [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C."). The U.S. also asserts sovereignty over five [unincorporated territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and [several uninhabited island possessions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands").<sup id="cite_ref-HRI-2012_232-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-HRI-2012-232"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOnuf2010xvii_233-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOnuf2010xvii-233"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>218<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. is the world's oldest surviving federation,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-234"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>219<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and its [presidential system of national government](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system") has been adopted, in whole or in part, by many newly independent states worldwide following their [decolonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decolonization "Decolonization").<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-235"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>220<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Constitution of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States") serves as [the country's supreme legal document](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supremacy_Clause "Supremacy Clause").<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-236"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>221<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Most scholars describe the United States as a liberal democracy.<sup id="cite_ref-Scheb_237-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Scheb-237"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>222<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-240"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>p<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### National government

Main article: [Federal government of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States "Federal government of the United States")

Composed of three branches, all headquartered in Washington, D.C., the federal government is the national government of the United States. It is regulated by a strong system of [checks and balances](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Checks_and_balances "Checks and balances").<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-241"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>225<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

- The [U.S. Congress](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Congress "United States Congress"), a [bicameral legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bicameral_legislature "Bicameral legislature") made up of the [Senate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Senate "United States Senate") and the [House of Representatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives "United States House of Representatives"), makes [federal law](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_law "Federal law"), [declares war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Declaration_of_war "Declaration of war"), approves treaties, has the [power of the purse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Power_of_the_purse "Power of the purse"),<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-242"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>226<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and has [the power of impeachment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Impeachment_in_the_United_States "Impeachment in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-243"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>227<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Senate has 100 members (2 from each state), elected for a six-year term. The House of Representatives has 435 members, each elected for a two-year term; all representatives serve one [congressional district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts "List of United States congressional districts") of equivalent population. Congressional districts are drawn by each state legislature and are contiguous within the state.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-244"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>228<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Congress also organizes a collection of [committees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_congressional_committee "United States congressional committee"), each of which handles a specific task or duty. One of Congress's foremost non-legislative functions is the power to [investigate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_investigation "Congressional investigation") and oversee the executive branch.<sup id="cite_ref-tws2010Sep11t11_245-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-tws2010Sep11t11-245"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>229<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Congressional oversight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_oversight "Congressional oversight") is usually delegated to committees and is facilitated by Congress's subpoena power.<sup id="cite_ref-tws2010Sep11t13_246-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-tws2010Sep11t13-246"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>230<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
- The U.S. president is the [head of state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Head_of_state "Head of state"), [commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-chief "Commander-in-chief") of the military, chief executive of the federal government, and has the ability to veto [legislative bills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_\(law\) "Bill (law)") from the U.S. Congress before they become law. However, [presidential vetoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Veto_power_in_the_United_States "Veto power in the United States") can be overridden by a two-thirds [supermajority](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supermajority#Use_in_governments_around_the_world "Supermajority") vote in both chambers of Congress. The president appoints the [members of the Cabinet](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_States "Cabinet of the United States"), subject to Senate approval, and names other officials who administer and enforce federal laws through [their respective agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_federal_agencies_in_the_United_States "List of federal agencies in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-247"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>231<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The president also has clemency power for federal crimes and [can issue pardons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_pardons_in_the_United_States "Federal pardons in the United States"). Finally, the president has the right to issue expansive "[executive orders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_orders "Executive orders")", subject to [judicial review](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_review_in_the_United_States "Judicial review in the United States"), in a number of policy areas. Candidates for president campaign with a vice-presidential [running mate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Running_mate "Running mate"). Both candidates are elected together, or defeated together, in a presidential election. Unlike other votes in American politics, this is technically an [indirect election](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indirect_election "Indirect election") in which the winner will be determined by the [U.S. Electoral College](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Electoral_College "United States Electoral College"). There, votes are officially cast by individual electors selected by [their state legislature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_legislature_\(United_States\) "State legislature (United States)").<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-248"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>232<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In practice, however, each of the 50 states chooses a group of presidential electors who are required to confirm the winner of their state's popular vote. Each state is allocated two electors plus one additional elector for each [congressional district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Congressional_district "Congressional district"), which in effect combines to equal the number of elected officials that state sends to Congress. The District of Columbia, with no representatives or senators, is allocated three electoral votes. Both the president and the vice president serve a four-year term, and the president may be [reelected to the office only once](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twenty-second Amendment to the United States Constitution"), for one additional four-year term.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-249"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>q<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
- The [U.S. federal judiciary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_judiciary_of_the_United_States "Federal judiciary of the United States"), whose judges are all appointed for life by the president with Senate approval, consists primarily of the [U.S. Supreme Court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States "Supreme Court of the United States"), the [U.S. courts of appeals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_courts_of_appeals "United States courts of appeals"), and the [U.S. district courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_district_court "United States district court"). The U.S. Supreme Court interprets laws and [overturn those they find unconstitutional](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Judicial_review "Judicial review").<sup id="cite_ref-FedJud_250-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FedJud-250"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Supreme Court has nine members led by the [Chief Justice of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_the_United_States "Chief Justice of the United States"). The members are appointed by the sitting president when a vacancy becomes available.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-251"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>234<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The first level in the federal courts is [federal district court](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_district_court "Federal district court") for any case under "[original jurisdiction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Original_jurisdiction#Federal_and_state_courts "Original jurisdiction")", such as federal statutes, the Constitution, or [treaties](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_treaty "International treaty"). There are twelve [federal circuits](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Courts_of_Appeals "United States Courts of Appeals") that divide the country into different regions for federal appeals courts. After a federal district court has decided a case, it can then be [appealed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Appellate_court "Appellate court") to a United States court of appeal. The next and highest court in the system is the Supreme Court of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-FedJud_250-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FedJud-250"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>233<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The three-branch system is known as the [presidential system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidential_system "Presidential system"), in contrast to the [parliamentary system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parliamentary_system "Parliamentary system"), where the executive is part of the legislative body. Many countries around the world imitated this aspect of the 1789 [Constitution of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constitution_of_the_United_States "Constitution of the United States"), especially in the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-Sundquist_252-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Sundquist-252"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>235<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Subdivisions

Main articles: [List of states and territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_states_and_territories_of_the_United_States "List of states and territories of the United States"), [List of federally recognized tribes by state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_federally_recognized_tribes_by_state "List of federally recognized tribes by state"), [U.S. state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._state "U.S. state"), [Indian country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_country "Indian country"), [Territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States"), and [County (United States)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/County_\(United_States\) "County (United States)")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Indian_reservations_in_the_Continental_United_States.png/250px-Indian_reservations_in_the_Continental_United_States.png)

Map of 326 [Indian reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_reservations_in_the_United_States "List of Indian reservations in the United States") in the United States; 231 recognized [Alaska Native tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Alaska_Native_tribal_entities "List of Alaska Native tribal entities") are not shown.

![Territories of the United States.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/United_States_%28%2Boverseas%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored_%28zoom%29.svg/330px-United_States_%28%2Boverseas%29%2C_administrative_divisions_-_en_-_colored_%28zoom%29.svg.png)

[Territories of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") include [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands"), [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), and the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands").

In the [U.S. federal system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalism_in_the_United_States "Federalism in the United States"), the sovereign powers are shared between three levels of government specified in the Constitution: the national government, the states, and Indian tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-3Sovereigns_253-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-3Sovereigns-253"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FelixSCohen_254-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FelixSCohen-254"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. also asserts sovereignty over five permanently inhabited territories: [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands"), [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), and the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands").<sup id="cite_ref-HRI-2012_232-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-HRI-2012-232"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Residents of the states are represented by their elected state and [local governments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States "Local government in the United States"), which are administrative divisions of the states.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-255"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>238<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> States are subdivided into counties or county equivalents, and [further divided into municipalities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Local_government_in_the_United_States "Local government in the United States"). The District of Columbia is [a federal district](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_district_of_the_United_States "Federal district of the United States") containing the U.S. capital, [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.")<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-256"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>239<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The federal district is an administrative division of the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-257"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>240<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Indian country is made up of 574 federally recognized tribes and 326 [Indian reservations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Indian_reservations_in_the_United_States "List of Indian reservations in the United States"). They hold a government-to-government relationship with the U.S. federal government in Washington and are legally defined as [domestic dependent nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Domestic_dependent_nations "Domestic dependent nations") with [inherent tribal sovereignty rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tribal_sovereignty_in_the_United_States "Tribal sovereignty in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-FelixSCohen_254-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FelixSCohen-254"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>237<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3Sovereigns_253-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-3Sovereigns-253"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>236<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-258"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>241<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:1_259-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-:1-259"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>242<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In addition to the five major territories, the U.S. also asserts sovereignty over the [United States Minor Outlying Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Minor_Outlying_Islands "United States Minor Outlying Islands") in the [Pacific Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pacific_Ocean "Pacific Ocean") and the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean").<sup id="cite_ref-HRI-2012_232-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-HRI-2012-232"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The seven undisputed islands without permanent populations are [Baker Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baker_Island "Baker Island"), [Howland Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Howland_Island "Howland Island"), [Jarvis Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jarvis_Island "Jarvis Island"), [Johnston Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Johnston_Atoll "Johnston Atoll"), [Kingman Reef](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingman_Reef "Kingman Reef"), [Midway Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midway_Atoll "Midway Atoll"), and [Palmyra Atoll](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmyra_Atoll "Palmyra Atoll"). U.S. sovereignty over the unpopulated [Bajo Nuevo Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bajo_Nuevo_Bank "Bajo Nuevo Bank"), [Navassa Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Navassa_Island "Navassa Island"), [Serranilla Bank](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serranilla_Bank "Serranilla Bank"), and [Wake Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wake_Island "Wake Island") is disputed.<sup id="cite_ref-HRI-2012_232-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-HRI-2012-232"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>217<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png/960px-Map_of_USA_with_state_and_territory_names_2.png)

### Political parties

Main articles: [Political parties in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_parties_in_the_United_States "Political parties in the United States"), [List of political parties in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_United_States "List of political parties in the United States"), and [Political party strength in U.S. states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_U.S._states "Political party strength in U.S. states")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/US_state_Legislature_and_Governor_Control.svg/250px-US_state_Legislature_and_Governor_Control.svg.png)

States and territories by partisan control, as of February 2025: 

  [Democratic Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_\(United_States\) "Democratic Party (United States)")

  [Republican Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_\(United_States\) "Republican Party (United States)")

  [New Progressive Party](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Progressive_Party_\(Puerto_Rico\) "New Progressive Party (Puerto Rico)")

  Divided partisan control

The Constitution is silent on political parties. However, they developed independently in the 18th century with the [Federalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalist_Party "Federalist Party") and [Anti-Federalist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anti-Federalist_Party "Anti-Federalist Party") parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Hofstadter-1969-iv_260-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Hofstadter-1969-iv-260"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>243<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Since then, the United States has operated as a *de facto* [two-party system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Two-party_system "Two-party system"), though the parties in that system have been different at different times.<sup id="cite_ref-Blake-2021_261-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Blake-2021-261"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>244<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The two main national parties are presently the [Democratic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Democratic_Party_\(United_States\) "Democratic Party (United States)") and the [Republican](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Republican_Party_\(United_States\) "Republican Party (United States)"). The former is perceived as [relatively liberal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States "Modern liberalism in the United States") in its [political platform](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_platform "Political platform") while the latter is perceived as [relatively conservative](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States "Conservatism in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-262"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>245<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Foreign relations

Main articles: [Foreign relations of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_United_States "Foreign relations of the United States") and [Foreign policy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_policy_of_the_United_States "Foreign policy of the United States")

![see caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/67%C2%BA_Per%C3%ADodo_de_Sesiones_de_la_Asamblea_General_de_Naciones_Unidas_%288020913157%29.jpg/250px-67%C2%BA_Per%C3%ADodo_de_Sesiones_de_la_Asamblea_General_de_Naciones_Unidas_%288020913157%29.jpg)

The [United Nations headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations") has been situated along the [East River](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_River "East River") in [Midtown Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midtown_Manhattan "Midtown Manhattan") since 1952; in 1945, the United States was a [founding member of the UN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_member_of_the_United_Nations "Founding member of the United Nations").

The United States has an established structure of foreign relations, and it has the world's [second-largest diplomatic corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_diplomatic_missions "List of countries by number of diplomatic missions") as of 2024. It is a [permanent member of the United Nations Security Council](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Permanent_members_of_the_United_Nations_Security_Council "Permanent members of the United Nations Security Council"),<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-263"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>246<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and home to the [United Nations headquarters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Headquarters_of_the_United_Nations "Headquarters of the United Nations").<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-264"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>247<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is a member of the [G7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G7 "G7"),<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-265"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>248<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [G20](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G20 "G20"),<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-266"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>249<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") intergovernmental organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-267"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>250<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Almost all countries have embassies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_in_the_United_States "List of diplomatic missions in the United States") and many have [consulates](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consul_\(representative\) "Consul (representative)") (official representatives) in the country. Likewise, nearly all countries host formal [diplomatic missions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diplomatic_mission "Diplomatic mission") with the United States, except [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Iran–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-268"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>251<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [North Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations "North Korea–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-269"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>252<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [Bhutan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Bhutan#Other_countries "Foreign relations of Bhutan").<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-270"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>253<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Though [Taiwan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taiwan%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Taiwan–United States relations") does not have formal diplomatic relations with the U.S., it maintains close unofficial relations.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-271"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>254<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States regularly [supplies Taiwan with military equipment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Six_Assurances "Six Assurances") to deter potential Chinese aggression.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-272"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>255<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Its geopolitical attention also turned to the [Indo-Pacific](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indo-Pacific "Indo-Pacific") when the United States joined the [Quadrilateral Security Dialogue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quadrilateral_Security_Dialogue "Quadrilateral Security Dialogue") with Australia, India, and Japan.<sup id="cite_ref-kobara_273-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-kobara-273"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>256<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has a "[Special Relationship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special_Relationship "Special Relationship")" [with the United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom%E2%80%93United_States_relations "United Kingdom–United States relations")<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-274"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>257<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and strong ties [with Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Canada–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-275"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>258<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Australia–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-276"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>259<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [New Zealand](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Zealand%E2%80%93United_States_relations "New Zealand–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-277"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>260<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [the Philippines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philippines%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Philippines–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-278"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>261<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Japan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japan%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Japan–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-279"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>262<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [South Korea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Korea%E2%80%93United_States_relations "South Korea–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-280"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>263<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Israel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israel%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Israel–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-281"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>264<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and several [European Union countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Member_state_of_the_European_Union "Member state of the European Union") ([France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France%E2%80%93United_States_relations "France–United States relations"), [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Italy–United States relations"), [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Germany–United States relations"), [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Spain–United States relations"), and [Poland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poland%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Poland–United States relations")).<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-282"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>265<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. works closely with its [NATO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NATO "NATO") allies on military and [national security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security "National security") issues, and with countries in the Americas through the [Organization of American States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organization_of_American_States "Organization of American States") and the [United States–Mexico–Canada Free Trade Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico%E2%80%93Canada_Agreement "United States–Mexico–Canada Agreement"). In South America, [Colombia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colombia "Colombia") is traditionally considered to be the closest ally of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-283"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>266<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. exercises full international defense authority and responsibility for [Micronesia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia "Federated States of Micronesia"), the [Marshall Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marshall_Islands "Marshall Islands"), and [Palau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palau "Palau") through the [Compact of Free Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Compact_of_Free_Association "Compact of Free Association").<sup id="cite_ref-FedJud_250-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FedJud-250"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>233<span
