class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It has increasingly conducted strategic cooperation [with India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India%E2%80%93United_States_relations "India–United States relations"),<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-284"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>267<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> while [its ties with China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China%E2%80%93United_States_relations "China–United States relations") have steadily deteriorated.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-285"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>268<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-286"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>269<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Since 2014, the U.S. has [become a key ally of Ukraine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ukraine%E2%80%93United_States_relations "Ukraine–United States relations").<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-287"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>270<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-288"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>271<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Military

Main article: [United States Armed Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Aerial_view_of_the_Pentagon%2C_Arlington%2C_VA_%2838285035892%29.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_the_Pentagon%2C_Arlington%2C_VA_%2838285035892%29.jpg)

[The Pentagon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon"), the headquarters of the [U.S. Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense") in [Arlington County, Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arlington_County,_Virginia "Arlington County, Virginia"), is one of the world's largest office buildings with over 6.5 million square feet (600,000 m<sup>2</sup>) of [floor space](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Floor_space "Floor space").

The president is the [commander-in-chief](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commander-in-Chief_of_the_United_States "Commander-in-Chief of the United States") of the United States Armed Forces and appoints its leaders, the [secretary of defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense "United States Secretary of Defense") and the [Joint Chiefs of Staff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff "Joint Chiefs of Staff"). The [Department of Defense](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Defense "United States Department of Defense"), which is headquartered at [the Pentagon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Pentagon "The Pentagon") near Washington, D.C., administers five of the six service branches, which are made up of the [U.S. Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Army "United States Army"), [Marine Corps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps "United States Marine Corps"), [Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Navy "United States Navy"), [Air Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Air_Force "United States Air Force"), and [Space Force](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Space_Force "United States Space Force").<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-289"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>272<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Coast Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Coast_Guard "United States Coast Guard") is administered by the [Department of Homeland Security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Homeland_Security "United States Department of Homeland Security") in peacetime and can be transferred to the [Department of the Navy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy "United States Department of the Navy") in wartime.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-290"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>273<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States [spent $916 billion on its military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_budget_of_the_United_States "Military budget of the United States") in 2023, which is by far the [largest amount of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_with_highest_military_expenditures "List of countries with highest military expenditures"), making up 37% of global military spending and accounting for 3.4% of the country's GDP.***<sup id="cite_ref-SIPRI-2020_291-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-SIPRI-2020-291"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>274<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>***<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-292"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>275<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. [possesses 42% of the world's nuclear weapons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_weapons_of_the_United_States "Nuclear weapons of the United States")—the second-largest stockpile after [that of Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia_and_weapons_of_mass_destruction "Russia and weapons of mass destruction").<sup id="cite_ref-Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute-2024_293-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute-2024-293"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>276<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has the [third-largest combined armed forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_military_and_paramilitary_personnel "List of countries by number of military and paramilitary personnel") in the world, behind the [Chinese People's Liberation Army](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army "People's Liberation Army") and [Indian Armed Forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Armed_Forces "Indian Armed Forces").<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-294"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>277<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The military operates about 800 bases and facilities abroad,<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-295"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>278<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and maintains [deployments greater than 100 active duty personnel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_military_deployments "United States military deployments") in 25 foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-296"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>279<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[State defense forces](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_defense_forces "State defense forces") (SDFs) are military units that operate under the sole authority of a state government. SDFs are authorized by state and federal law but are under the command of [the state's governor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Governor_\(United_States\) "Governor (United States)").<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-297"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>280<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-298"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>281<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-299"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>282<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They are distinct from the state's [National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Guard_\(United_States\) "National Guard (United States)") units in that they cannot become federalized entities. A state's National Guard personnel, however, may be federalized under the [National Defense Act Amendments of 1933](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Defense_Act_of_1916#National_Defense_Act_Amendments_of_1933 "National Defense Act of 1916"), which created the Guard and provides for the integration of [Army National Guard](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Army_National_Guard "Army National Guard") units and personnel into the U.S. Army and (since 1947) the U.S. Air Force.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-300"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>283<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Law enforcement and criminal justice

Main articles: [Law of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_of_the_United_States "Law of the United States"), [Law enforcement in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_the_United_States "Law enforcement in the United States"), and [Crime in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crime_in_the_United_States "Crime in the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Washington_DC%2C_FBI_-_panoramio.jpg/250px-Washington_DC%2C_FBI_-_panoramio.jpg)

[J. Edgar Hoover Building](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._Edgar_Hoover_Building "J. Edgar Hoover Building"), the headquarters of the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation") (FBI), in [Washington, D.C.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington,_D.C. "Washington, D.C.")

There are about 18,000 U.S. police agencies from local to national level in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-301"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>284<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Law in the United States is mainly enforced by local police departments and [sheriff departments](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sheriffs_in_the_United_States "Sheriffs in the United States") in their municipal or county jurisdictions. [The state police](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_police_\(United_States\) "State police (United States)") departments [have authority in their respective state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Police_power_\(United_States_constitutional_law\) "Police power (United States constitutional law)"), and [federal agencies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_law_enforcement_in_the_United_States "Federal law enforcement in the United States") such as the [Federal Bureau of Investigation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Investigation "Federal Bureau of Investigation") (FBI) and the [U.S. Marshals Service](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Marshals_Service "United States Marshals Service") have national jurisdiction and specialized duties, such as protecting [civil rights](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Civil_rights "Civil rights"), [national security](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_security_of_the_United_States "National security of the United States") and enforcing [U.S. federal courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._federal_courts "U.S. federal courts")' rulings and federal laws.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-302"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>285<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [State courts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_court_\(United_States\) "State court (United States)") conduct most civil and criminal trials,<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-303"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>286<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and federal courts handle designated crimes and [appeals of state court decisions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_courts_of_appeals "United States courts of appeals").<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-304"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>287<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

There is no unified "criminal justice system" in the United States. The [American prison system](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incarceration_in_the_United_States "Incarceration in the United States") is largely heterogenous, with thousands of relatively independent systems operating across federal, state, local, and tribal levels. In 2024, "these systems hold [over 1.9 million people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Incarceration_in_the_United_States "Incarceration in the United States") in 1,566 state prisons, 98 federal prisons, 3,116 local jails, 1,323 juvenile correctional facilities, 142 immigration detention facilities, and 80 Indian country jails, as well as in [military prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._military_prisons "List of U.S. military prisons"), civil commitment centers, state psychiatric hospitals, and prisons in the U.S. territories."<sup id="cite_ref-Sawyer-2024_305-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Sawyer-2024-305"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>288<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Despite disparate systems of confinement, four main institutions dominate: [federal prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_United_States_federal_prisons "List of United States federal prisons"), [state prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lists_of_United_States_state_prisons "Lists of United States state prisons"), local jails, and [juvenile correctional facilities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_juvenile_justice_system "American juvenile justice system").<sup id="cite_ref-National_Academies_Press-2014_306-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-306"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Federal prisons are run by the [Federal Bureau of Prisons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federal_Bureau_of_Prisons "Federal Bureau of Prisons") and hold people who have been convicted of federal crimes, including pretrial detainees.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Academies_Press-2014_306-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-306"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> State prisons, run by the official department of correction of each state, hold sentenced people serving prison time (usually longer than one year) for felony offenses.<sup id="cite_ref-National_Academies_Press-2014_306-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-306"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Local jails are county or municipal facilities that incarcerate defendants prior to trial; they also hold those serving short sentences (typically under a year).<sup id="cite_ref-National_Academies_Press-2014_306-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-National_Academies_Press-2014-306"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>289<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Juvenile correctional facilities are operated by local or state governments and serve as longer-term placements for any minor adjudicated as delinquent and ordered by a judge to be confined.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-307"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>290<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In January 2023, the United States had the [sixth-highest per capita incarceration rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_incarceration_rate "List of countries by incarceration rate") in the world—531 people per 100,000 inhabitants—and the largest prison and jail population in the world, with more than 1.9 million people incarcerated.<sup id="cite_ref-Sawyer-2024_305-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Sawyer-2024-305"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>288<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-308"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>291<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WorldPrisonBrief_309-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-WorldPrisonBrief-309"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>292<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> An analysis of the [World Health Organization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Health_Organization "World Health Organization") Mortality Database from 2010 showed U.S. homicide rates "were 7 times higher than in other high-income countries, driven by [a gun homicide rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gun_deaths_in_the_United_States "Gun deaths in the United States") that was 25 times higher".<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-310"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>293<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Economy

Main article: [Economy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy_of_the_United_States "Economy of the United States")

![see caption](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/US_one_dollar_bill%2C_obverse%2C_series_2009.jpg/250px-US_one_dollar_bill%2C_obverse%2C_series_2009.jpg)

The [U.S. dollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar") is the most-used currency [in international transactions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_use_of_the_U.S._dollar "International use of the U.S. dollar") and the world's foremost [reserve currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reserve_currency "Reserve currency").<sup id="cite_ref-federalreserve.gov_311-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-federalreserve.gov-311"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The U.S. economy has been the world's [largest nominally since about 1890](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_largest_historical_GDP "List of countries by largest historical GDP").<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-312"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>295<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 2024 U.S. [gross domestic product](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_domestic_product "Gross domestic product") (GDP) of more than $29 trillion<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-313"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>296<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PPP_19-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-PPP-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>e<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> was the highest in the world, constituting over 25% of the nominal [global economic output](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gross_world_product "Gross world product") or 15% at [purchasing power parity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity "Purchasing power parity") (PPP). From 1983 to 2008, U.S. real compounded annual GDP growth was 3.3%, compared to a 2.3% weighted average for the rest of the [G7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/G7 "G7").<sup id="cite_ref-Hagopian_314-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Hagopian-314"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>297<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The country ranks [first in the world by nominal GDP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(nominal\) "List of countries by GDP (nominal)"),<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-315"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>298<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [second when adjusted for purchasing power parities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(PPP\) "List of countries by GDP (PPP)") (PPP),<sup id="cite_ref-IMFWEO.US_20-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-IMFWEO.US-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [ninth by PPP-adjusted GDP per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_\(PPP\)_per_capita "List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita").<sup id="cite_ref-IMFWEO.US_20-5" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-IMFWEO.US-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It has the [highest disposable household income per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Disposable_household_and_per_capita_income#Disposable_income_per_capita_\(OECD\) "Disposable household and per capita income") among [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") countries.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-316"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>299<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In February 2024, the total [U.S. federal government debt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_debt_of_the_United_States "National debt of the United States") was $34.4 trillion.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-317"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>300<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Aerial_view_of_Apple_Park_dllu.jpg/250px-Aerial_view_of_Apple_Park_dllu.jpg)

[Apple Inc.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_Inc. "Apple Inc."), one of the world's [biggest companies by market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_public_corporations_by_market_capitalization "List of public corporations by market capitalization"),<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-318"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>301<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> has its global headquarters in [Cupertino, California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cupertino,_California "Cupertino, California").

Of the world's [500 largest companies by revenue](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fortune_Global_500 "Fortune Global 500"), [136 were headquartered in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_companies_in_the_United_States_by_revenue "List of largest companies in the United States by revenue") in 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-Fortune-2022_319-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Fortune-2022-319"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>302<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> which is the highest number of any country.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-320"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>303<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [U.S. dollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar "United States dollar") is the currency most used [in international transactions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_use_of_the_U.S._dollar "International use of the U.S. dollar") and is the world's foremost [reserve currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reserve_currency "Reserve currency"), backed by the country's dominant economy, [its military](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces "United States Armed Forces"), the [petrodollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petrodollar "Petrodollar") system, and its linked [eurodollar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eurodollar "Eurodollar") and large [U.S. treasuries market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Treasury "U.S. Treasury").<sup id="cite_ref-federalreserve.gov_311-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-federalreserve.gov-311"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>294<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Several countries use it as their official currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_dollar#Countries_that_use_US_dollar "United States dollar"), and in others it is the [*de facto* currency](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/De_facto_currency "De facto currency").<sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin_J._Cohen_2006,_p._17_321-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Benjamin_J._Cohen_2006,_p._17-321"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>304<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-322"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>305<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. has [free trade agreements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade_agreements "Free trade agreements") with [several countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Free_trade_agreements_of_the_United_States "Free trade agreements of the United States"), including the [USMCA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Mexico%E2%80%93Canada_Agreement "United States–Mexico–Canada Agreement").<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-323"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>306<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It ranked second in the [Global Competitiveness Report](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Competitiveness_Report "Global Competitiveness Report") in 2019, after Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Economic_Forum_324-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-World_Economic_Forum-324"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>307<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Although the United States has reached a [post-industrial level of development](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Post-industrial_economy "Post-industrial economy")<sup id="cite_ref-Collins-2023_325-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Collins-2023-325"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>308<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and is often described as having a [service economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Service_economy "Service economy"),<sup id="cite_ref-Collins-2023_325-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Collins-2023-325"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>308<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Econ_326-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Econ-326"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>309<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> it remains a major industrial power.<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-327"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>310<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2021, the [U.S. manufacturing sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._manufacturing_sector "U.S. manufacturing sector") was the world's [second-largest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_manufacturing_output "List of countries by manufacturing output") after China's.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-328"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>311<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Gaming-Wall-Street_BTS_Prodigium-266.jpg/250px-Gaming-Wall-Street_BTS_Prodigium-266.jpg)

The [New York Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange "New York Stock Exchange") on [Wall Street](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wall_Street "Wall Street"), the world's [largest stock exchange by market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges#Major_stock_exchanges "List of stock exchanges")<sup id="cite_ref-NYSEhighestcap_329-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NYSEhighestcap-329"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>312<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[New York City](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_City "New York City") is the world's principal [financial center](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_center "Financial center")<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-330"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>313<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYCFintechAndFinancialCapitalWorld_331-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NYCFintechAndFinancialCapitalWorld-331"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>314<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the epicenter of the world's [largest metropolitan economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP "List of cities by GDP").<sup id="cite_ref-NYCEpicenterUSMetroEconomy_332-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-NYCEpicenterUSMetroEconomy-332"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>315<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [New York Stock Exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange "New York Stock Exchange") and [Nasdaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasdaq "Nasdaq"), both located in New York City, are the world's two [largest stock exchanges](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges "List of stock exchanges") by [market capitalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Market_capitalization "Market capitalization") and [trade volume](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trade_volume "Trade volume").<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-333"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>316<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sfc.hk_334-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-sfc.hk-334"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>317<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is at or near the forefront of [technological advancement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_United_States "Science and technology in the United States") and [innovation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Innovation "Innovation")<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-335"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>318<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> in many economic fields, especially in [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence"); [electronics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electronics "Electronics") and [computers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer "Computer"); [pharmaceuticals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmaceuticals "Pharmaceuticals"); and medical, [aerospace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerospace "Aerospace") and [military equipment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Military_equipment "Military equipment").<sup id="cite_ref-CIA-2018_194-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CIA-2018-194"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The country's economy is fueled by abundant [natural resources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource "Natural resource"), a well-developed [infrastructure](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Infrastructure_policy_of_the_United_States "Infrastructure policy of the United States"), and [high productivity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_labour_productivity "List of countries by labour productivity").<sup id="cite_ref-Wright,_Gavin_2007_p._185_336-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Wright,_Gavin_2007_p._185-336"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>319<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [largest trading partners of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_the_largest_trading_partners_of_the_United_States "List of the largest trading partners of the United States") are the [European Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/European_Union "European Union"), Mexico, Canada, China, Japan, South Korea, the United Kingdom, Vietnam, India, and Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-337"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>320<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is the world's [largest importer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_imports "List of countries by imports") and [second-largest exporter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_exports "List of countries by exports").<sup id="cite_ref-340" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-340"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>r<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It is by far the world's [largest exporter of services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_service_exports "List of countries by service exports").<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-341"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>323<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Americans have the highest average [household](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Household_income "Household income") and [employee income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_average_wage "List of countries by average wage") among OECD member states,<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-342"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>324<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the fourth-highest [median household income](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median_income "Median income") in 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-343"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>325<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> up from sixth-highest in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Household_Income_344-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Household_Income-344"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>326<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> With personal [consumption expenditures](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumer_spending "Consumer spending") of over $18.5 trillion in 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-345"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>327<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the U.S. has a heavily [consumer-driven economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consumer_economy "Consumer economy") and is the world's [largest consumer market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_consumer_markets "List of largest consumer markets").<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-346"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>328<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. [ranked first in the number of dollar billionaires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_billionaires "List of countries by number of billionaires") and [millionaires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_millionaires "List of countries by number of millionaires") in 2023, with 735 billionaires and nearly 22 million millionaires.<sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-347"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>329<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[Wealth in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_in_the_United_States "Wealth in the United States") is highly concentrated; in 2011, the richest 10% of the adult population owned 72% of the country's household wealth, while the bottom 50% owned just 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-348"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>330<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [U.S. wealth inequality](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wealth_inequality_in_the_United_States "Wealth inequality in the United States") increased substantially since the late 1980s,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_349-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-:0-349"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>331<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [income inequality in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Income_inequality_in_the_United_States "Income inequality in the United States") reached a record high in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-350"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>332<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By 2024, the country had some of the highest wealth and income inequality among [OECD](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OECD "OECD") countries.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-351"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>333<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Since the 1970s, there has been a decoupling of U.S. wage gains from worker productivity.<sup id="cite_ref-Hopkin_352-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Hopkin-352"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>334<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2016, the top fifth of earners took home more than half of all income,<sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-353"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>335<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> giving the U.S. one of the widest income distributions among OECD countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Sme_354-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Sme-354"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>336<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hopkin_352-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Hopkin-352"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>334<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> There were about 771,480 [homeless persons in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homelessness_in_the_United_States "Homelessness in the United States") in 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-355"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>337<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, 6.4 million children experienced food insecurity.<sup id="cite_ref-ers.usda.gov_356-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-ers.usda.gov-356"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>338<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Feeding America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feeding_America "Feeding America") estimates that around one in five, or approximately 13 million, [children experience hunger in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunger_in_the_United_States#Children "Hunger in the United States") and do not know where they will get their next meal or when.<sup id="cite_ref-FactsAbout_357-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FactsAbout-357"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>339<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Also in 2022, about 37.9 million people, or 11.5% of the U.S. population, were [living in poverty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Poverty_in_the_United_States "Poverty in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-358"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>340<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has a smaller [welfare state](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Welfare_state "Welfare state") and redistributes less income through government action than most other [high-income countries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy "World Bank high-income economy").<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-359"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>341<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-360" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-360"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>342<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It is the only [advanced economy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Advanced_economy "Advanced economy") that does not [guarantee its workers paid vacation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_statutory_minimum_employment_leave_by_country "List of statutory minimum employment leave by country") nationally<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-361"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>343<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and is one of a few countries in the world without federal [paid family leave](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parental_leave_in_the_United_States "Parental leave in the United States") as a legal right.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-362"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>344<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States has a higher percentage of low-income [workers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Working_class_in_the_United_States "Working class in the United States") than almost any other developed country, largely because of a weak [collective bargaining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collective_bargaining "Collective bargaining") system and lack of government support for at-risk workers.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-363"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>345<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Science and technology

Main article: [Science and technology in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_the_United_States "Science and technology in the United States")

The United States [has been a leader in technological innovation since the late 19th century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Technological_and_industrial_history_of_the_United_States "Technological and industrial history of the United States") and scientific research since the mid-20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-364"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>346<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Methods for producing [interchangeable parts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interchangeable_parts "Interchangeable parts") and the establishment of a [machine tool](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_tool "Machine tool") industry enabled [the large-scale manufacturing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_system_of_manufacturing "American system of manufacturing") of U.S. consumer products in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-365"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>347<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> By the early 20th century, factory [electrification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Electrification "Electrification"), the introduction of the [assembly line](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Assembly_line "Assembly line"), and other [labor-saving techniques](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automation "Automation") created the system of [mass production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mass_production "Mass production").<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-366"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>348<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In the 21st century, the United States continues to be one of the world's foremost scientific powers,<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-367"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>349<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> though China has emerged as a major competitor in many fields.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-368"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>350<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. has the [highest total research and development expenditure of any country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_by_research_and_development_spending "List of sovereign states by research and development spending")<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-369"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>351<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and ranks ninth as a percentage of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-370"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>352<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, the United States was (after China) the country with the [second-highest number of published scientific papers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_number_of_scientific_and_technical_journal_articles "List of countries by number of scientific and technical journal articles").<sup id="cite_ref-371" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-371"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>353<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2021, the U.S. ranked second (also after China) by the number of patent applications, and third by trademark and industrial design applications (after China and Germany), according to [World Intellectual Property Indicators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Intellectual_Property_Indicators "World Intellectual Property Indicators").<sup id="cite_ref-372" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-372"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>354<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2023 and 2024, the United States ranked third (after Switzerland and Sweden) in the [Global Innovation Index](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Innovation_Index "Global Innovation Index").<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-373"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>355<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-374"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>356<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is considered to be the leading country in the development of [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence") technology.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-375"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>357<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2023, the United States was ranked the second most technologically advanced country in the world (after South Korea) by *[Global Finance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Finance_\(magazine\) "Global Finance (magazine)")* magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-376"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>358<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Spaceflight

Main article: [Space policy of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_policy_of_the_United_States "Space policy of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag-crop.jpg/250px-Buzz_salutes_the_U.S._Flag-crop.jpg)

U.S. astronaut [Buzz Aldrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buzz_Aldrin "Buzz Aldrin") saluting the [American flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States "Flag of the United States") on the [Moon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon "Moon") during the 1969 [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") mission; the United States is the only country that has [landed crews on the lunar surface](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing").

The United States has maintained a space program since the late 1950s, beginning with the establishment of the [National Aeronautics and Space Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASA "NASA") (NASA) in 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-377"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>359<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-378"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>360<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> NASA's [Apollo program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_program "Apollo program") (1961–1972) achieved the first crewed [Moon landing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moon_landing "Moon landing") with the 1969 [Apollo 11](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apollo_11 "Apollo 11") mission; it remains one of the agency's most significant milestones.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-379"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>361<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-380"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>362<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Other major endeavors by NASA include the [Space Shuttle program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program "Space Shuttle program") (1981–2011),<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-381"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>363<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the [Voyager program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Voyager_program "Voyager program") (1972–present), the [Hubble](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope "Hubble Space Telescope") and [James Webb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_Webb_Space_Telescope "James Webb Space Telescope") [space telescopes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Space_telescope "Space telescope") (launched in 1990 and 2021, respectively),<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-382"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>364<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-383"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>365<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the multi-mission [Mars Exploration Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Program "Mars Exploration Program") (*[Spirit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mars_Exploration_Rover "Mars Exploration Rover")* and *[Opportunity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Opportunity_\(rover\) "Opportunity (rover)")*, *[Curiosity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Curiosity_\(rover\) "Curiosity (rover)"),* and *[Perseverance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perseverance_\(rover\) "Perseverance (rover)")*).<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-384"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>366<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> NASA is one of five agencies collaborating on the [International Space Station](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Space_Station "International Space Station") (ISS);<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-385"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>367<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> U.S. contributions to the ISS include several modules, including *[Destiny](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Destiny_\(ISS_module\) "Destiny (ISS module)")* (2001), *[Harmony](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harmony_\(ISS_module\) "Harmony (ISS module)")* (2007), and *[Tranquility](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tranquility_\(ISS_module\) "Tranquility (ISS module)")* (2010), as well as ongoing logistical and operational support.<sup id="cite_ref-386" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-386"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>368<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States [private sector](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_sector "Private sector") dominates the global [commercial spaceflight industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Private_spaceflight "Private spaceflight").<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-387"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>369<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Prominent American spaceflight contractors include [Blue Origin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blue_Origin "Blue Origin"), [Boeing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boeing "Boeing"), [Lockheed Martin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lockheed_Martin "Lockheed Martin"), [Northrop Grumman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northrop_Grumman "Northrop Grumman"), and [SpaceX](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/SpaceX "SpaceX"). NASA programs such as the [Commercial Crew Program](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Crew_Program "Commercial Crew Program"), [Commercial Resupply Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Resupply_Services "Commercial Resupply Services"), [Commercial Lunar Payload Services](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Commercial_Lunar_Payload_Services "Commercial Lunar Payload Services"), and [NextSTEP](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Next_Space_Technologies_for_Exploration_Partnerships "Next Space Technologies for Exploration Partnerships") have facilitated growing private-sector involvement in American spaceflight.<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-388"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>370<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Energy

Main article: [Energy in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Energy_in_the_United_States "Energy in the United States")

In 2023, the United States received approximately 84% of its energy from fossil fuel, and the largest source of the country's energy came from [petroleum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petroleum_in_the_United_States "Petroleum in the United States") (38%), followed by [natural gas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_gas_in_the_United_States "Natural gas in the United States") (36%), [renewable sources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renewable_energy_in_the_United_States "Renewable energy in the United States") (9%), [coal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coal_in_the_United_States "Coal in the United States") (9%), and [nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_in_the_United_States "Nuclear power in the United States") (9%).<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-389"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>371<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-visu_390-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-visu-390"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>372<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, the United States constituted only about 4% of the [world's population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_population "World population"), but consumed around 16% of the [world's energy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_energy_consumption "World energy consumption").<sup id="cite_ref-391" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-391"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>373<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The U.S. ranks as the [second-highest emitter of greenhouse gases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_greenhouse_gas_emissions "List of countries by greenhouse gas emissions") behind China.<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-392"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>374<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The U.S. is the world's [largest producer of nuclear power](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuclear_power_by_country "Nuclear power by country"), generating around 30% of the world's nuclear electricity.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-393"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>375<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It also has the highest number of nuclear power reactors of any country.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-394"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>376<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> From 2024, the U.S. plans to triple its nuclear power capacity by 2050.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-395"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>377<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Transportation

Main article: [Transportation in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_in_the_United_States "Transportation in the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/45intoI-10_2.jpg/250px-45intoI-10_2.jpg)

Interchange between [Interstate 10](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_10 "Interstate 10") and [Interstate 45](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_45 "Interstate 45") in [Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Houston "Houston"), Texas

The [automotive industry in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_the_United_States "Automotive industry in the United States") is the [second-largest by motor vehicle manufacturing output](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_motor_vehicle_production "List of countries by motor vehicle production"), having dominated the world market for much of the twentieth century. [Detroit, Michigan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Detroit,_Michigan "Detroit, Michigan"), is still referred to as "Motor City" because of its historical significance as the center of the American automobile industry, having been home to America's "[Big Three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Big_Three_\(automobile_manufacturers\) "Big Three (automobile manufacturers)")" car manufacturers for a long time. The U.S. is in the top ten countries for [highest vehicle ownership per capita](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_vehicles_per_capita "List of countries by vehicles per capita"), with 850 vehicles per 1000 people in 2022. The 4 million miles (6.4 million kilometers) road network, owned almost entirely by state and local governments, is the [longest in the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_road_network_size "List of countries by road network size").<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-396"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>378<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-397"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>379<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The extensive [Interstate Highway System](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_Highway_System "Interstate Highway System") connects all major cities and is funded mostly by the federal government but maintained by [state departments of transportation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_and_insular_area_departments_of_transportation "List of U.S. state and insular area departments of transportation"), supplemented by state expressways and some private [toll roads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toll_road "Toll road").

A 2022 study found that 76% of U.S. commuters drive alone and 14% ride a bicycle, including bike owners and users of [bike-sharing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bike-sharing "Bike-sharing") networks. About 11% use some form of public transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-398"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>380<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-399"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>381<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Public transportation in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Public_transportation_in_the_United_States "Public transportation in the United States") is well developed in the largest urban areas, notably New York City, Chicago, Boston, Philadelphia, and Portland, Oregon; otherwise, coverage is generally less extensive than in most other developed countries. The U.S. also has many relatively [car-dependent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car-dependent "Car-dependent") localities.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-400"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>382<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Long-distance intercity travel is provided primarily by airlines, but travel by rail is more common along the [Northeast Corridor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_Corridor "Northeast Corridor"), the only [high-speed rail in the U.S.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_the_United_States "High-speed rail in the United States") that meets international standards. [Amtrak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amtrak "Amtrak"), the country's government-sponsored national passenger rail company, has a relatively sparse network compared to that of Western European countries. Service is concentrated in the Northeast, Illinois, and the West Coast.

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Atlanta_Hartsfield-Jackson_%28cropped%29.jpg/250px-Atlanta_Hartsfield-Jackson_%28cropped%29.jpg)

[Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport "Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport"), serving the [Atlanta metropolitan area](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_metropolitan_area "Atlanta metropolitan area"), is the world's [busiest airport by passenger traffic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic "List of busiest airports by passenger traffic") with over 75 million passengers as of 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-401"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>383<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-402"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>384<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has an extensive air transportation network, and the country accounted for just over half of the world's [aerospace production](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aerospace_production "Aerospace production") in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-403"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>385<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [U.S. civilian airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airlines_of_the_United_States "List of airlines of the United States") are all privately owned. The three largest airlines in the world, by total number of passengers carried, are U.S.-based; [American Airlines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Airlines "American Airlines") became the global leader after its 2013 merger with [US Airways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/US_Airways "US Airways").<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-404"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>386<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Among the busiest 50 airports in the world, 16 are in the United States, as well as five of the top 10.<sup id="cite_ref-PANYNJ_2021_report_405-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-PANYNJ_2021_report-405"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>387<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The world's busiest airport by passenger volume is [Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hartsfield%E2%80%93Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport "Hartsfield–Jackson Atlanta International Airport") in [Atlanta, Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta "Atlanta").<sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-406"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>388<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PANYNJ_2021_report_405-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-PANYNJ_2021_report-405"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>387<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, most of the [19,969 U.S. airports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_States "List of airports in the United States")<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-407"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>389<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> were owned and operated by local government authorities, and there are also some private airports. Some 5,193 are designated as "public use", including for [general aviation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_aviation "General aviation"). The [Transportation Security Administration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_Security_Administration "Transportation Security Administration") has provided security at most major airports since 2001.

[The country's rail transport network](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_States "Rail transport in the United States"), the [longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_rail_transport_network_size "List of countries by rail transport network size") in the world at 182,412.3 mi (293,564.2 km),<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-408"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>390<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> handles mostly [freight](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Freight_transport "Freight transport")<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-409"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>391<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-410"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>392<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> (in contrast to more passenger-centered rail in Europe<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-411"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>393<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>). Because they are often privately owned operations as well, U.S. railroads lag behind those of the rest of the world in terms of electrification.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-412"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>394<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Of the world's [50 busiest container ports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_busiest_container_ports "List of busiest container ports"), four are located in the United States, with the busiest in the U.S. being the [Port of Los Angeles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Port_of_Los_Angeles "Port of Los Angeles").<sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-413"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>395<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

[The country's inland waterways](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inland_waterways_of_the_United_States "Inland waterways of the United States") are the world's [fifth-longest](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_waterways_length "List of countries by waterways length"), totaling 41,009 km (25,482 mi).<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-414"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>396<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They are used extensively for freight, recreation, and a small amount of passenger traffic. [Miami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miami "Miami") is a major international hub for [cruise ship](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cruise_ship "Cruise ship") and airline passengers visiting the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean").

[Transportation in Alaska](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transportation_in_Alaska "Transportation in Alaska") relies more on airplanes, ferries, [all-terrain vehicles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle "All-terrain vehicle"), and [snowmobiles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowmobile "Snowmobile") because many settlements are not connected to the contiguous North American road network. Long distances and the requirements of the [Jones Act](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jones_Act "Jones Act") result in higher transportation costs for [Hawaii](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaii "Hawaii") and [insular areas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Insular_area "Insular area") from the rest of the United States.

## Demographics

Main article: [Demographics of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States "Demographics of the United States")

### Population

Main articles: [Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americans "Americans") and [Race and ethnicity in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_and_ethnicity_in_the_United_States "Race and ethnicity in the United States")

See also: [List of U.S. states by population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_population "List of U.S. states by population")

| State | Population (millions) |
| --- | --- |
| [California](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California "California") | 39.4 |
| [Texas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas "Texas") | 31.3 |
| [Florida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Florida "Florida") | 23.4 |
| [New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_\(state\) "New York (state)") | 19.9 |
| [Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pennsylvania "Pennsylvania") | 13.1 |
| [Illinois](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Illinois "Illinois") | 12.7 |
| [Ohio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ohio "Ohio") | 11.9 |
| [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_\(U.S._state\) "Georgia (U.S. state)") | 11.2 |
| [North Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Carolina "North Carolina") | 11.0 |
| [Michigan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michigan "Michigan") | 10.1 |

The [U.S. Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau") reported 331,449,281 residents on April 1, 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-417"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>t<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2020CENSUS_418-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-2020CENSUS-418"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>398<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> making the United States the [third-most-populous country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population "List of countries and dependencies by population") in the world, after China and India.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA-2018_194-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CIA-2018-194"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>179<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Census Bureau's official 2024 population estimate was 340,110,988, an increase of 2.6% since the 2020 census.<sup id="cite_ref-Vintage_2024_419-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Vintage_2024-419"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>399<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> According to the Bureau's [U.S. Population Clock](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._and_World_Population_Clock "U.S. and World Population Clock"), on July 1, 2024, the U.S. population had a net gain of one person every 16 seconds, or about 5400 people per day.<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-420"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>400<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2023, 51% of Americans age 15 and over were married, 6% were [widowed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Widowed "Widowed"), 10% were divorced, and 34% had never been married.<sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-421"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>401<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2023, the [total fertility rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Total_fertility_rate "Total fertility rate") for the U.S. stood at 1.6 children per woman,<sup id="cite_ref-422" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-422"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>402<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and, at 23%, it had the world's highest rate of children living in [single-parent](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Single_parents_in_the_United_States "Single parents in the United States") households in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-423"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>403<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has a diverse population; 37 [ancestry groups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_ancestries "American ancestries") have more than one million members.<sup id="cite_ref-An2000_424-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-An2000-424"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>404<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [White Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-Hispanic_whites "Non-Hispanic whites") with ancestry from Europe, the Middle East, or North Africa form the largest [racial](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Race_\(human_classification\) "Race (human classification)") and [ethnic group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group "Ethnic group") at 57.8% of the United States population.<sup id="cite_ref-425" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-425"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>405<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-426" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-426"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>406<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Hispanic and Latino Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans "Hispanic and Latino Americans") form the second-largest group and are 18.7% of the United States population. [African Americans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_Americans "African Americans") constitute the country's third-largest ancestry group and are 12.1% of the total U.S. population.<sup id="cite_ref-An2000_424-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-An2000-424"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>404<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Asian Americans are the country's fourth-largest group, composing 5.9% of the United States population. The country's 3.7 million Native Americans account for about 1%,<sup id="cite_ref-An2000_424-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-An2000-424"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>404<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and some 574 native tribes are recognized by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-427" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-427"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>407<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2022, the [median age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Median_age "Median age") of the United States population was 38.9 years.<sup id="cite_ref-428" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-428"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>408<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Language

Main article: [Languages of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Languages_of_the_United_States "Languages of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Languages_cp-02.svg/250px-Languages_cp-02.svg.png)

Most spoken languages in the U.S.

While many languages are spoken in the United States, [English](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_English "American English") is by far the most commonly spoken and written.<sup id="cite_ref-429" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-429"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>409<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> English was made the [official language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_language "Official language") of the United States by [Executive Order 14224](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_14224 "Executive Order 14224") in 2025.<sup id="cite_ref-EOWP_4-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-EOWP-4"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, Congress has never passed a bill to designate English as the official language of all three federal branches. Some laws, such as [U.S. naturalization requirements](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Naturalized_citizen_of_the_United_States "Naturalized citizen of the United States"), nonetheless standardize English. Twenty-eight states and the [United States Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Virgin_Islands "United States Virgin Islands") have declared English as the sole official language; 19 states and the [District of Columbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/District_of_Columbia "District of Columbia") have no official language.<sup id="cite_ref-430" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-430"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>410<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Three states and four U.S. territories have recognized local or indigenous languages in addition to English: Hawaii ([Hawaiian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawaiian_language "Hawaiian language")),<sup id="cite_ref-431" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-431"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>411<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Alaska ([twenty Native languages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alaska_Native_languages "Alaska Native languages")),<sup id="cite_ref-432" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-432"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>u<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-433" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-433"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>412<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> South Dakota ([Sioux](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sioux_language "Sioux language")),<sup id="cite_ref-LakotaCommon_434-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-LakotaCommon-434"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>413<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> American Samoa ([Samoan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samoan_language "Samoan language")), Puerto Rico ([Spanish](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_United_States "Spanish language in the United States")), Guam ([Chamorro](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chamorro_language "Chamorro language")), and the Northern Mariana Islands ([Carolinian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carolinian_language "Carolinian language") and Chamorro). In total, 169 Native American languages are spoken in the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-435" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-435"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>414<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In Puerto Rico, Spanish is more widely spoken than English.<sup id="cite_ref-PuertoRicoTranslation_436-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-PuertoRicoTranslation-436"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>415<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
