class="cite-bracket">[</span>555<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [rhythm and blues](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues "Rhythm and blues") in the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014§_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages28-4-popular-culture-and-mass-media_28.4]_578-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOpenStax2014%C2%A7_[httpsopenstaxorgbooksus-historypages28-4-popular-culture-and-mass-media_28.4]-578"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>556<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the 1960s, [Bob Dylan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Dylan "Bob Dylan") emerged from the [folk revival](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_folk_music_revival "American folk music revival") to become one of the country's most celebrated songwriters.<sup id="cite_ref-579" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-579"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>557<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The musical forms of [punk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punk_rock "Punk rock") and [hip hop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hip_hop "Hip hop") both originated in the United States in the 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-580" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-580"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>558<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The United States has the world's [largest music market](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_recorded_music_markets "List of largest recorded music markets"), with a total retail value of $15.9 billion in 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-581" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-581"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>559<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Most of the world's [major record companies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Record_label#Major_labels "Record label") are based in the U.S.; they are represented by the [Recording Industry Association of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America "Recording Industry Association of America") (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-582" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-582"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>560<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Mid-20th-century American pop stars, such as [Frank Sinatra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Sinatra "Frank Sinatra")<sup id="cite_ref-583" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-583"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>561<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [Elvis Presley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elvis_Presley "Elvis Presley"),<sup id="cite_ref-584" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-584"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>562<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> became [global celebrities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Superstar "Superstar") and [best-selling music artists](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists "List of best-selling music artists"),<sup id="cite_ref-Biddle-2001_575-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Biddle-2001-575"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>553<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> as have artists of the late 20th century, such as [Michael Jackson](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Jackson "Michael Jackson"),<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_585-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-RIAA-585"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>563<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Madonna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madonna "Madonna"),<sup id="cite_ref-586" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-586"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>564<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Whitney Houston](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Whitney_Houston "Whitney Houston"),<sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone-2023_587-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Rolling_Stone-2023-587"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>565<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [Mariah Carey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariah_Carey "Mariah Carey"),<sup id="cite_ref-588" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-588"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>566<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the early 21st century, such as [Eminem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eminem "Eminem"),<sup id="cite_ref-589" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-589"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>567<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Britney Spears](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Britney_Spears "Britney Spears"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490_590-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-590"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>568<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Lady Gaga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lady_Gaga "Lady Gaga"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490_590-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-590"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>568<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Katy Perry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katy_Perry "Katy Perry"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490_590-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEdmondson2013490-590"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>568<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Taylor Swift](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor_Swift "Taylor Swift") and [Beyoncé](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9 "Beyoncé").<sup id="cite_ref-591" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-591"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>569<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Fashion

Main article: [Fashion in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_in_the_United_States "Fashion in the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Carolina_Herrera_AW14_12.jpg/250px-Carolina_Herrera_AW14_12.jpg)

[Haute couture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haute_couture "Haute couture") [fashion models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_model "Fashion model") on the [catwalk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Catwalk "Catwalk") during [New York Fashion Week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week "New York Fashion Week")

The United States has the world's largest [apparel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apparel "Apparel") market by revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-592" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-592"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>570<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Apart from professional [business attire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Business_attire "Business attire"), American fashion is eclectic and predominantly informal. Americans' diverse cultural roots are reflected in their clothing; however, [sneakers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sneaker "Sneaker"), [jeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jeans "Jeans"), [T-shirts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/T-shirts "T-shirts"), and [baseball caps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baseball_cap "Baseball cap") are emblematic of American styles.<sup id="cite_ref-AmericanClassicFashion_593-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-AmericanClassicFashion-593"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>571<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> New York, with [its fashion week](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Fashion_Week "New York Fashion Week"), is considered to be one of the "Big Four" global [fashion capitals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fashion_capital "Fashion capital"), along with [Paris](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris_Fashion_Week "Paris Fashion Week"), [Milan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Milan_Fashion_Week "Milan Fashion Week"), and [London](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London_Fashion_Week "London Fashion Week"). A study demonstrated that general proximity to [Manhattan's Garment District](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Garment_District,_Manhattan "Garment District, Manhattan") has been synonymous with American fashion since its inception in the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-GarmentDistrictNYCFashionSymbolUS_594-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-GarmentDistrictNYCFashionSymbolUS-594"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>572<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The headquarters of many [designer labels](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Designer_label "Designer label") reside in [Manhattan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manhattan "Manhattan"). Labels cater to [niche markets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Niche_market "Niche market"), such as preteens. New York Fashion Week is one of the most influential fashion weeks in the world, and occurs twice a year;<sup id="cite_ref-USNYCFashionWeekGlobalIndustryTonesetter_595-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-USNYCFashionWeekGlobalIndustryTonesetter-595"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>573<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> while the annual [Met Gala](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Met_Gala "Met Gala") in Manhattan is commonly known as the fashion world's "biggest night".<sup id="cite_ref-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight1_596-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight1-596"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>574<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight2_597-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-MetGalaFashion'sBiggestNight2-597"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>575<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Cinema

Main article: [Cinema of the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cinema_of_the_United_States "Cinema of the United States")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg/250px-Hollywood_Sign_%28Zuschnitt%29.jpg)

The iconic [Hollywood Sign](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Sign "Hollywood Sign") in the [Hollywood Hills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood_Hills "Hollywood Hills"), often regarded as the symbol of the [American film industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_film_industry "American film industry")

The U.S. film industry has [a worldwide influence and following](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Global_Hollywood "Global Hollywood"). [Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hollywood,_Los_Angeles "Hollywood, Los Angeles"), a district in northern Los Angeles, the nation's second-most populous city, is also [metonymous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metonymous "Metonymous") for the American filmmaking industry.<sup id="cite_ref-598" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-598"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>576<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-599" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-599"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>577<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-600" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-600"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>578<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [major film studios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_film_studios "Major film studios") of the United States are the primary source of the [most commercially successful](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films "List of highest-grossing films") and most ticket-selling movies in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Kerrigan_Page_18_601-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kerrigan_Page_18-601"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>579<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Davis_602-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Davis-602"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>580<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Since the early 20th century, the U.S. film industry has largely been based in and around Hollywood, although in the 21st century an increasing number of films are not made there, and film companies have been subject to the forces of globalization.<sup id="cite_ref-603" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-603"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>581<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [Academy Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Awards "Academy Awards"), popularly known as the Oscars, have been held annually by the [Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_of_Motion_Picture_Arts_and_Sciences "Academy of Motion Picture Arts and Sciences") since 1929,<sup id="cite_ref-DrowneHuber2004_604-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-DrowneHuber2004-604"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>582<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and the [Golden Globe Awards](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award "Golden Globe Award") have been held annually since January 1944.<sup id="cite_ref-Kroon2014_605-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kroon2014-605"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>583<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The industry peaked in what is commonly referred to as the "[Golden Age of Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Hollywood_cinema "Classical Hollywood cinema")", from the early sound period until the early 1960s,<sup id="cite_ref-606" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-606"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>584<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> with screen actors such as [John Wayne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Wayne "John Wayne") and [Marilyn Monroe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marilyn_Monroe "Marilyn Monroe") becoming iconic figures.<sup id="cite_ref-607" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-607"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>585<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-608" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-608"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>586<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the 1970s, "[New Hollywood](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Hollywood "New Hollywood")", or the "Hollywood Renaissance",<sup id="cite_ref-Greven2013_609-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Greven2013-609"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>587<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> was defined by grittier films influenced by French and Italian realist pictures of the [post-war period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_II "Aftermath of World War II").<sup id="cite_ref-Morrison1998_610-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Morrison1998-610"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>588<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 21st century has been marked by the rise of American streaming platforms, which came to rival traditional cinema.<sup id="cite_ref-RE_611-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-RE-611"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>589<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-612" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-612"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>590<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Cuisine

Main article: [American cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_cuisine "American cuisine")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/2019-11-28_14_46_15_A_single_serving_of_Thanksgiving_Dinner_in_the_Parkway_Village_section_of_Ewing_Township%2C_Mercer_County%2C_New_Jersey.jpg/250px-2019-11-28_14_46_15_A_single_serving_of_Thanksgiving_Dinner_in_the_Parkway_Village_section_of_Ewing_Township%2C_Mercer_County%2C_New_Jersey.jpg)

A [Thanksgiving dinner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thanksgiving_dinner "Thanksgiving dinner") with [roast turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roast_turkey "Roast turkey"), [mashed potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashed_potatoes "Mashed potatoes"), [pickles](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pickled_cucumber "Pickled cucumber"), [corn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Corn "Corn"), [candied yams](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candied_yams "Candied yams"), [cranberry jelly](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cranberry_jelly "Cranberry jelly"), [shrimps](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shrimp_and_prawn_as_food "Shrimp and prawn as food"), [stuffing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stuffing "Stuffing"), [green peas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_peas "Green peas"), [deviled eggs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deviled_eggs "Deviled eggs"), [green salad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_salad "Green salad"), and [apple sauce](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_sauce "Apple sauce")

Early settlers were introduced by Native Americans to foods such as [turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey_as_food "Turkey as food"), [sweet potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sweet_potato "Sweet potato"), [corn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maize "Maize"), [squash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cucurbita "Cucurbita"), and [maple syrup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maple_syrup "Maple syrup"). Of the most enduring and pervasive examples are variations of the native dish called [succotash](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Succotash "Succotash"). Early settlers and later immigrants combined these with foods they were familiar with, such as [wheat flour](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wheat_flour "Wheat flour"),<sup id="cite_ref-Wheat_613-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Wheat-613"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>591<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> beef, and milk, to create a distinctive American cuisine.<sup id="cite_ref-614" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-614"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>592<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-615" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-615"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>593<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [New World crops](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_World_crops "New World crops"), especially [pumpkin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pumpkin "Pumpkin"), corn, [potatoes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Potatoes "Potatoes"), and turkey as the main course are part of a shared national menu on [Thanksgiving](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thanksgiving_\(United_States\) "Thanksgiving (United States)"), when many Americans prepare or purchase traditional dishes to celebrate the occasion.<sup id="cite_ref-Mintz1996_616-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Mintz1996-616"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>594<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Characteristic American dishes such as [apple pie](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Apple_pie "Apple pie"), [fried chicken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fried_chicken "Fried chicken"), [doughnuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doughnut "Doughnut"), [french fries](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_fries "French fries"), [macaroni and cheese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macaroni_and_cheese "Macaroni and cheese"), [ice cream](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_cream "Ice cream"), [hamburgers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hamburger "Hamburger"), [hot dogs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_dog "Hot dog"), and [American pizza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pizza_in_the_United_States "Pizza in the United States") derive from the recipes of various immigrant groups.<sup id="cite_ref-617" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-617"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>595<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-618" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-618"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>596<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-619" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-619"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>597<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-620" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-620"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>598<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Mexican dishes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican-American_cuisine "Mexican-American cuisine") such as [burritos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Burritos "Burritos") and [tacos](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tacos "Tacos") preexisted the United States in areas later annexed from Mexico, and [adaptations of Chinese cuisine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Chinese_cuisine "American Chinese cuisine") as well as [pasta dishes freely adapted from Italian sources](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian-American_cuisine "Italian-American cuisine") are all widely consumed.<sup id="cite_ref-IFT_621-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-IFT-621"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>599<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> American [chefs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chef "Chef") have had a significant impact on society both domestically and internationally. In 1946, the [Culinary Institute of America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culinary_Institute_of_America "Culinary Institute of America") was founded by [Katharine Angell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katharine_Cramer_Angell "Katharine Cramer Angell") and [Frances Roth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frances_Roth "Frances Roth"). This would become the United States' most prestigious culinary school, where many of the most talented American chefs would study prior to successful careers.<sup id="cite_ref-622" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-622"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>600<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FTfbs_623-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FTfbs-623"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>601<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The [United States restaurant industry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_restaurant_industry "United States restaurant industry") was projected at $899 billion in sales for 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-Brownfield-2020_624-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Brownfield-2020-624"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>602<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ramirez_625-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Ramirez-625"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>603<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and employed more than 15 million people, representing 10% of the nation's workforce directly.<sup id="cite_ref-Brownfield-2020_624-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Brownfield-2020-624"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>602<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It is the country's second-largest private employer and the third-largest employer overall.<sup id="cite_ref-Noguchi-2020_626-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Noguchi-2020-626"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>604<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-627" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-627"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>605<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States is home to over 220 [Michelin star](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michelin_star "Michelin star")\-rated restaurants, 70 of which are in New York City alone.<sup id="cite_ref-628" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-628"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>606<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Wine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_wine "American wine") has been produced in what is now the United States since the 1500s, with the [first widespread production beginning in what is now New Mexico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Mexico_wine "New Mexico wine") in 1628.<sup id="cite_ref-629" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-629"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>607<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Birchell_Steel_2013_p._630-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Birchell_Steel_2013_p.-630"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>608<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-New_Mexico._Office_of_Cultural_Affairs_1995_p._631-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-New_Mexico._Office_of_Cultural_Affairs_1995_p.-631"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>609<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the modern U.S., wine production is undertaken in all fifty states, with [California producing 84 percent of all U.S. wine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/California_wine "California wine"). With more than 1,100,000 acres (4,500 km<sup>2</sup>) under vine, the United States is the [fourth-largest wine-producing country](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_countries_by_wine_production "List of countries by wine production") in the world, after [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italian_wine "Italian wine"), [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spanish_wine "Spanish wine"), and [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_wine "French wine").<sup id="cite_ref-Sotheby,_p._462_632-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Sotheby,_p._462-632"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>610<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oxford,_p._719_633-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Oxford,_p._719-633"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>611<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

The American [fast-food](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast-food "Fast-food") industry developed alongside the nation's [car culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Car_culture "Car culture").<sup id="cite_ref-634" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-634"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>612<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> American restaurants developed the [drive-in](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drive-in "Drive-in") format in the 1920s, which they began to replace with the [drive-through](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drive-through "Drive-through") format by the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-drivethru_635-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-drivethru-635"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>613<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-636" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-636"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>614<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> American [fast-food restaurant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fast-food_restaurant "Fast-food restaurant") chains, such as [McDonald's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/McDonald%27s "McDonald's"), [Kentucky Fried Chicken](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kentucky_Fried_Chicken "Kentucky Fried Chicken"), [Dunkin' Donuts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dunkin%27_Donuts "Dunkin' Donuts") and [many others](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_fast_food_restaurant_chains#United_States "List of fast food restaurant chains"), have numerous outlets around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Pavlova-2019_637-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Pavlova-2019-637"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>615<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

### Sports

Main articles: [Sports in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_in_the_United_States "Sports in the United States") and [United States at the Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_Olympics "United States at the Olympics")

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Commanders_vs._Jaguars_%2852379056543%29.jpg/250px-Commanders_vs._Jaguars_%2852379056543%29.jpg)

[American football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football "American football") is the most popular sport in the United States; in this September 2022 [National Football League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_League "National Football League") game, the [Jacksonville Jaguars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars "Jacksonville Jaguars") play the [Washington Commanders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Washington_Commanders "Washington Commanders") at [FedExField](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FedExField "FedExField").

The most popular spectator sports in the U.S. are [American football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football_in_the_United_States "American football in the United States"), [basketball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basketball_in_the_United_States "Basketball in the United States"), [baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baseball_in_the_United_States "Baseball in the United States"), [soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soccer_in_the_United_States "Soccer in the United States"), and [ice hockey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ice_hockey_in_the_United_States "Ice hockey in the United States").<sup id="cite_ref-638" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-638"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>616<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> While most major U.S. sports such as baseball and American football have evolved out of European practices, basketball, [volleyball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Volleyball_in_the_United_States "Volleyball in the United States"), [skateboarding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Skateboarding "Skateboarding"), and [snowboarding](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Snowboarding "Snowboarding") are American inventions, many of which have become popular worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-639" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-639"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>617<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> [Lacrosse](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lacrosse_in_the_United_States "Lacrosse in the United States") and [surfing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surfing_in_the_United_States "Surfing in the United States") arose from Native American and Native Hawaiian activities that predate European contact.<sup id="cite_ref-liss_640-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-liss-640"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>618<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [market for professional sports in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Professional_sports_market_in_the_United_States "Professional sports market in the United States") was approximately $69 billion in July 2013, roughly 50% larger than that of Europe, the Middle East, and Africa combined.<sup id="cite_ref-641" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-641"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>619<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

American football is by several measures the most popular spectator sport in the United States;<sup id="cite_ref-642" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-642"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>620<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the [National Football League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_League "National Football League") has the highest average attendance of any sports league in the world, and the [Super Bowl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl "Super Bowl") is watched by tens of millions globally.<sup id="cite_ref-643" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-643"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>621<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, baseball has been regarded as the U.S. "[national sport](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_sport "National sport")" since the late 19th century. After American football, the next four most popular professional team sports are basketball, baseball, soccer, and ice hockey. Their premier leagues are, respectively, the [National Basketball Association](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Basketball_Association "National Basketball Association"), [Major League Baseball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Baseball "Major League Baseball"), [Major League Soccer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Soccer "Major League Soccer"), and the [National Hockey League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Hockey_League "National Hockey League"). The most-watched [individual sports](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Individual_sport "Individual sport") in the U.S. are [golf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golf_in_the_United_States "Golf in the United States") and [auto racing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auto_racing "Auto racing"), particularly [NASCAR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NASCAR "NASCAR") and [IndyCar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IndyCar "IndyCar").<sup id="cite_ref-644" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-644"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>622<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-645" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-645"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>623<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

On the [collegiate level](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_athletics_in_the_United_States "College athletics in the United States"), earnings for the member institutions exceed $1 billion annually,<sup id="cite_ref-si_646-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-si-646"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>624<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and [college football](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_football "College football") and [basketball](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_basketball "College basketball") attract large audiences, as the [NCAA March Madness tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_men%27s_basketball_tournament "NCAA Division I men's basketball tournament") and the [College Football Playoff](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_Football_Playoff "College Football Playoff") are some of the most watched national sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-647" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-647"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>625<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In the U.S., the intercollegiate sports level serves as a feeder system for professional sports. This differs greatly from practices in nearly all other countries, where publicly and privately funded sports organizations serve this function.<sup id="cite_ref-648" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-648"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>626<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

Eight [Olympic Games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Olympic_Games "Olympic Games") have taken place in the United States. The [1904 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1904_Summer_Olympics "1904 Summer Olympics") in [St. Louis, Missouri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis,_Missouri "St. Louis, Missouri"), were the first-ever Olympic Games held outside of Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-649" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-649"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>627<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Olympic Games will be held in the U.S. for a ninth time when Los Angeles hosts the [2028 Summer Olympics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2028_Summer_Olympics "2028 Summer Olympics"). [U.S. athletes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_Olympics "United States at the Olympics") have won a total of 2,968 medals (1,179 gold) at the Olympic Games, the most of any country.<sup id="cite_ref-650" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-650"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>628<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-651" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-651"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>629<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-652" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-652"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>630<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

In international professional competition, the [U.S. men's national soccer team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team "United States men's national soccer team") has qualified for [eleven World Cups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_FIFA_World_Cup "United States at the FIFA World Cup"), while the [women's national team](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_soccer_team "United States women's national soccer team") has [won](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_at_the_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "United States at the FIFA Women's World Cup") the [FIFA Women's World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "FIFA Women's World Cup") and [Olympic soccer tournament](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Football_at_the_Summer_Olympics "Football at the Summer Olympics") four times each.<sup id="cite_ref-653" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-653"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>631<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The United States hosted the [1994 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup "1994 FIFA World Cup") and will co-host, along with Canada and Mexico, the [2026 FIFA World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup "2026 FIFA World Cup").<sup id="cite_ref-654" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-654"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>632<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The [1999 FIFA Women's World Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup "1999 FIFA Women's World Cup") was also hosted by the United States. [Its final match](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1999_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_final "1999 FIFA Women's World Cup final") was watched by 90,185, setting the world record for most-attended women's sporting event at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-655" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-655"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>633<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>

## Notes

1. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-officiallanguage_6-0 "Jump up")** Declared by [Executive Order 14224](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Executive_Order_14224 "Executive Order 14224"), not by legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-EOWP_4-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-EOWP-4"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-EONYT_5-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-EONYT-5"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> States and territories variously recognize English only, English plus one or more local languages, or no language at all. See [§ Language](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#Language).
2. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-demonym_11-0 "Jump up")** The historical and informal demonym [Yankee](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yankee "Yankee") has been applied to Americans, New Englanders, or northeasterners since the 18th century.
3. ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-1) [<sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-largestcountry_15-2) At 3,531,900 sq mi (9,147,590 km<sup>2</sup>), the United States is the third-largest country in the world by land area, behind [Russia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russia "Russia") and [China](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China "China"). By total area (land and water), it is the third-largest, behind Russia and [Canada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canada "Canada"), if its coastal and territorial water areas are included. However, if only its internal waters are included (bays, sounds, rivers, lakes, and the [Great Lakes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Great_Lakes "Great Lakes")), the U.S. is the fourth-largest, after Russia, Canada, and China.  
	Coastal/territorial waters included: 3,796,742 sq mi (9,833,517 km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>  
	Only internal waters included: 3,696,100 sq mi (9,572,900 km<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
4. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-pop_17-0 "Jump up")** Excludes [Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico") and the other [unincorporated islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States "Unincorporated territories of the United States") because they are counted separately in [U.S. census](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._census "U.S. census") statistics
5. ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-PPP_19-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-PPP_19-1) U.S. nominal and PPP-adjusted GDP are the same as the U.S. is the reference country for PPP calculations.
6. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-21 "Jump up")** After adjustment for taxes and transfers
7. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-time_24-0 "Jump up")** See [Time in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_in_the_United_States "Time in the United States") for details about laws governing time zones in the United States.
8. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-25 "Jump up")** See [Date and time notation in the United States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Date_and_time_notation_in_the_United_States "Date and time notation in the United States").
9. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-drive_27-0 "Jump up")** The [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands "U.S. Virgin Islands") use left-hand traffic.
10. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-28 "Jump up")** While the state of Hawaii is not geographically part of North America, it is associated politically with the continent as part of the U.S.
11. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-pop_clock_31-0 "Jump up")** The [U.S. Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau")'s latest official population estimate of 340,110,988 residents (2024) is for the 50 states and the District of Columbia; it excludes the 3.6 million residents of the five major [U.S. territories](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States "Territories of the United States") and outlying islands. The Census Bureau also provides a continuously updated but unofficial population clock: [www.census.gov/popclock](https://www.census.gov/popclock/)
12. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-37 "Jump up")** The official [U.S. Government Publishing Office Style Manual](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Government_Publishing_Office_Style_Manual "U.S. Government Publishing Office Style Manual") has prescribed specific usages for "U.S." and "United States" as part of official names. In "formal writing (treaties, Executive orders, proclamations, etc.); congressional bills; legal citations and courtwork; and covers and title pages",<sup id="cite_ref-gpo-stylemanual_36-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-gpo-stylemanual-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "United States" is always used. In a sentence containing the name of another country, "United States" must be used. Otherwise, "U.S." is used preceding a government organization or as an adjective, but "United States" is used as an adjective preceding non-governmental organizations (e.g. [United States Steel Corporation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Steel_Corporation "United States Steel Corporation")).<sup id="cite_ref-gpo-stylemanual_36-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-gpo-stylemanual-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
13. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-41 "Jump up")** *Americus* comes from the [Medieval Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin "Medieval Latin") name *Emericus* (for [Saint Emeric of Hungary](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint_Emeric_of_Hungary "Saint Emeric of Hungary")), itself derived from the Old High German name [Emmerich](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmerich_\(name\) "Emmerich (name)").
14. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-70 "Jump up")** From the late 15th century, the [Columbian exchange](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Columbian_exchange "Columbian exchange") had been catastrophic for native populations throughout the Americas. It is estimated [that up to 95 percent of the indigenous populations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virgin_soil_epidemic "Virgin soil epidemic"), especially in the Caribbean, [perished from infectious diseases during the years following European colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Native_American_disease_and_epidemics "Native American disease and epidemics");<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> remaining populations were often displaced by European expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJoseph2016590_68-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJoseph2016590-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
15. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-74 "Jump up")** [New Hampshire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_New_Hampshire "Province of New Hampshire"), [Massachusetts](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_Massachusetts_Bay "Province of Massachusetts Bay"), [Connecticut](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Connecticut_Colony "Connecticut Colony"), [Rhode Island](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Rhode_Island_and_Providence_Plantations "Colony of Rhode Island and Providence Plantations"), [New York](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_New_York "Province of New York"), [New Jersey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_New_Jersey "Province of New Jersey"), [Pennsylvania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania "Province of Pennsylvania"), [Delaware](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Delaware_Colony "Delaware Colony"), [Maryland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_Maryland "Province of Maryland"), [Virginia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colony_of_Virginia "Colony of Virginia"), [North Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_North_Carolina "Province of North Carolina"), [South Carolina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_South_Carolina "Province of South Carolina"), and [Georgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Province_of_Georgia "Province of Georgia")
16. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-240 "Jump up")** Some scholars have used descriptions such as [oligarchy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oligarchy#United_States "Oligarchy") or [plutocracy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plutocracy#Post-World_War_II "Plutocracy") instead.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-238"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>223<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kroll_2010-12-02_239-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-Kroll_2010-12-02-239"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>224<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
17. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-249 "Jump up")** Per the [U.S. Constitution, Amendment Twenty-three](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Twenty-third_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution "Twenty-third Amendment to the United States Constitution"), proposed by the U.S. Congress on June 16, 1960, and ratified by the States on March 29, 1961
18. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-340 "Jump up")** A country's total exports are usually understood to be goods and services. Based on this, the U.S. is the world's second-largest exporter, after China.<sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-338"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>321<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, if primary income is included, the U.S. is the world's largest exporter.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-339"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>322<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
19. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-416 "Jump up")** These population figures are official 2024 annual estimates (rounded off) from the [U.S. Census Bureau](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau "United States Census Bureau").<sup id="cite_ref-CensusEst2024_415-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_note-CensusEst2024-415"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>397<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
20. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-417 "Jump up")** This figure, like most official data for the United States as a whole, excludes the five unincorporated territories ([Puerto Rico](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Puerto_Rico "Puerto Rico"), [Guam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guam "Guam"), the [U.S. Virgin Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/U.S._Virgin_Islands "U.S. Virgin Islands"), [American Samoa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Samoa "American Samoa"), and the [Northern Mariana Islands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands "Northern Mariana Islands")) and minor island possessions.
21. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-432 "Jump up")** [Inupiaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inupiaq_language "Inupiaq language"), [Siberian Yupik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Siberian_Yupik_language "Central Siberian Yupik language"), [Central Alaskan Yup'ik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language "Central Alaskan Yup'ik language"), [Alutiiq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alutiiq_language "Alutiiq language"), [Unanga](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aleut_language "Aleut language") (Aleut), [Denaʼina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dena%CA%BCina_language "Denaʼina language"), [Deg Xinag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deg_Xinag_language "Deg Xinag language"), [Holikachuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holikachuk_language "Holikachuk language"), [Koyukon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Koyukon_language "Koyukon language"), [Upper Kuskokwim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Kuskokwim_language "Upper Kuskokwim language"), [Gwichʼin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gwich%CA%BCin_language "Gwichʼin language"), [Tanana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lower_Tanana_language "Lower Tanana language"), [Upper Tanana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Tanana_language "Upper Tanana language"), [Tanacross](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanacross_language "Tanacross language"), [Hän](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/H%C3%A4n_language "Hän language"), [Ahtna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahtna_language "Ahtna language"), [Eyak](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eyak_language "Eyak language"), [Tlingit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tlingit_language "Tlingit language"), [Haida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haida_language "Haida language"), and [Tsimshian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coast_Tsimshian_dialect "Coast Tsimshian dialect")
22. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-470 "Jump up")** Also known less formally as Obamacare

95. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-110 "Jump up")**
	- [Meyer et al. 2001](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#CITEREFMeyerSnowSnowCohen2001), From 1800 to 1900: "The discovery of gold in California in 1848 proved a momentous watershed for native people in the West. Hordes of single men stampeded to find fortune. Unrestrained by family, community, or church, they decimated the native population near the goldfields. California natives suffered the most complete genocide in U.S. history."
	- Wolf, Jessica. ["Revealing the history of genocide against California's Native Americans"](https://newsroom.ucla.edu/stories/revealing-the-history-of-genocide-against-californias-native-americans). *UCLA Newsroom*. Retrieved July 8, 2018.
	- Madley, Benjamin (2016). [*An American Genocide: The United States and the California Indian Catastrophe, 1846-1873*](https://archive.org/details/americangenocide0000madl). Yale University Press. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_\(identifier\) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-0-300-23069-7](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-300-23069-7 "Special:BookSources/978-0-300-23069-7").
	- [Smithers 2012](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#CITEREFSmithers2012), p. 339: "The genocidal intent of California settlers and government officials was acted out in numerous battles and massacres (and aided by technological advances in weaponry, especially after the Civil War), in the abduction and sexual abuse of Indian women, and in the economic exploitation of Indian child labourers"
	- [Blackhawk 2023](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#CITEREFBlackhawk2023), p. 38: "With these works, a near consensus emerged. By most scholarly definitions and consistent with the UN Convention, these scholars all asserted that genocide against at least some Indigenous peoples had occurred in North America following colonisation, perpetuated first by colonial empires and then by independent nation-states"

177. **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/#cite_ref-Multiple_Sources_192-0 "Jump up")** 
	- Harvey, Michael (2022). "Introduction: History's Rhymes". In Harvey, Michael (ed.). [*Donald Trump in Historical Perspective*](https://www.taylorfrancis.com/chapters/edit/10.4324/9781003110361-1/introduction-michael-harvey). Routledge. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.4324/9781003110361-1](https://doi.org/10.4324%2F9781003110361-1). [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_\(identifier\) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-1-003-11036-1](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-003-11036-1 "Special:BookSources/978-1-003-11036-1"). As with the Beer Hall Putsch, a would-be leader tried to take advantage of an already scheduled event (in Hitler's case, Kahr's speech; in Trump's, Congress's tallying of the electoral votes) to create a dramatic moment with himself at the center of attention, calling for bold action to upend the political order. Unlike Hitler's coup attempt, Trump already held top of office, so he was attempting to hold onto power, not seize it (the precise term for Trump's intended action is a 'self-coup' or 'autogolpe'). Thus, Trump was able to plan for the event well in advance, and with much greater control, including developing the legal arguments that could be used to justify rejecting the election's results. (p. 3)
	- Pion-Berlin, David; Bruneau, Thomas; Goetze, Richard B. Jr. (April 7, 2022). ["The Trump self-coup attempt: comparisons and civil–military relations"](https://doi.org/10.1017%2Fgov.2022.13). *Government and Opposition*. **58** (4): 789–806\. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1017/gov.2022.13](https://doi.org/10.1017%2Fgov.2022.13). [S2CID](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/S2CID_\(identifier\) "S2CID (identifier)") [248033246](https://api.semanticscholar.org/CorpusID:248033246).
	- Castañeda, Ernesto; Jenks, Daniel (April 17, 2023). Costa, Bruno Ferreira; Parton, Nigel (eds.). ["January 6th and De-Democratization in the United States"](https://doi.org/10.3390%2Fsocsci12040238). *Social Sciences*. **12** (4). [MDPI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MDPI "MDPI"): 238. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_\(identifier\) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.3390/socsci12040238](https://doi.org/10.3390%2Fsocsci12040238). [ISSN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISSN_\(identifier\) "ISSN (identifier)") [2076-0760](https://search.worldcat.org/issn/2076-0760). What the United States went through on January 6th was an attempt at a self-coup, where Trump would use force to stay as head of state even if abandoning democratic practices in the U.S. Some advised Trump to declare martial law to create a state of emergency and use that as an excuse to stay in power.
	- Eisen, Norman; Ayer, Donald; Perry, Joshua; Bookbinder, Noah; Perry, E. Danya (June 6, 2022). [Trump on Trial: A Guide to the January 6 Hearings and the Question of Criminality](https://www.brookings.edu/research/trump-on-trial/) (Report). Brookings Institution. Retrieved December 16, 2023. \[Trump\] tried to delegitimize the election results by disseminating a series of far fetched and evidence-free claims of fraud. Meanwhile, with a ring of close confidants, Trump conceived and implemented unprecedented schemes to – in his own words – "overturn" the election outcome. Among the results of this "Big Lie" campaign were the terrible events of January 6, 2021 – an inflection point in what we now understand was nothing less than an attempted coup.
	- *Eastman v Thompson, et al.*, [8:22-cv-00099-DOC-DFM Document 260](https://storage.courtlistener.com/recap/gov.uscourts.cacd.841840/gov.uscourts.cacd.841840.260.0.pdf), 44 (S.D. Cal. May 28, 2022) ("Dr. Eastman and President Trump launched a campaign to overturn a democratic election, an action unprecedented in American history. Their campaign was not confined to the ivory tower – it was a coup in search of a legal theory. The plan spurred violent attacks on the seat of our nation's government, led to the deaths of several law enforcement officers, and deepened public distrust in our political process... If Dr. Eastman and President Trump's plan had worked, it would have permanently ended the peaceful transition of power, undermining American democracy and the Constitution. If the country does not commit to investigating and pursuing accountability for those responsible, the Court fears January 6 will repeat itself.").
